b.  A detailed map indicating all areas proposed to be served, and a proposed time schedule for the installation of all equipment necessary to become operational throughout the entire area to be serviced; 
c.  A statement or schedule setting forth all proposed classifications or rates and charges to be made against subscribers and all rates and charges as to each of such classifications, including installation charges, cable service charges, and any other telecommunications service charges; 
d.  A detailed, informative, and referenced statement describing the actual equipment and operational standards proposed by the applicant; 
e.  A copy of the form of any agreement, undertaking, or other instrument proposed to be entered into between the applicant and any subscriber to cable or telecommunications services; and 
f.  A detailed statement setting forth in its entirety any and all agreements and undertakings, whether formal or informal, written, oral, or implied, existing or proposed to exist between the applicant and any person, firm, or corporation which materially relate or pertain to or depend upon the application and the granting of the franchise; 
(4)  A copy of any agreement covering the franchise area, if existing between the applicant and any utility providing for the use of any facilities of the utility including, but not limited to, poles, lines or conduits; and 
(5)  Any other details, statements, supplementary information, or references pertinent to the subject matter of such application which shall be required or requested by the mayor and council, or by any other provision of law. 
(Code 2002, § 26-33; Ord. of 5-14-2001(2), § 10-7-3) 
Sec. 30-22. - Nonrefundable application fees for new franchises. 
(a)  Generally. No application for a new franchise shall be considered without payment by the applicant of application fees as provided in this section. If a franchise is granted, application fees will not be deemed a credit towards any other fees or sums due by the grantee. If an application is denied, the application fee will not be refunded. 
(b)  Purpose of fees. The application fees provided by this section will serve to cover the direct and indirect costs incurred by the city in processing the application, evaluating the applicant, and granting a franchise, and shall include, but not be limited to, administrative, engineering, publication, legal and consultant's expenses. 
(c)  Furnishing by applicant. The applicant will be expected to pay the reasonable costs of the city in evaluating the application. Notwithstanding any other requirement of this article, each applicant must furnish with its proposal a nonrefundable application fee in an amount as shall be determined by the mayor and council from time to time, by certified check or cashier's check made payable to the city. 
(Code 2002, § 26-34; Ord. of 5-14-2001(2), § 10-7-4) 
Sec. 30-23. - Responsibilities of applicants. 
It shall be the responsibility of each applicant for a franchise to comply with all applicable laws, ordinances, resolutions, rules, regulations and other directives of the city and any federal, state or local governmental authority having jurisdiction. 
(Code 2002, § 26-35; Ord. of 5-14-2001(2), § 10-7-5) 
Sec. 30-24. - Public availability of applications. 
To the extent determined by the mayor and council, applications for franchises, including any additions, modifications or amendments thereto, shall be available for public inspection at a designated city office during normal business hours. 
(Code 2002, § 26-36; Ord. of 5-14-2001(2), § 10-7-6) 
Sec. 30-25. - Evaluation criteria. 
In making any determination under this article as to any application for a franchise, the mayor and council may consider such factors as it deems appropriate and in the public interest including, without limitation: 
(1)  The adequacy of the proposed compensation to be paid to the city, including the value of any facilities and telecommunications services offered by the applicant to the city; 
(2)  The legal, financial, technical and other appropriate qualifications of the applicant; 
(3)  The ability of the applicant to maintain the property of the city in good condition throughout the term of the franchise; 
(4)  The value and efficiency to the city and its residents of the cable services and other telecommunications services to be provided, including the type of telecommunications services to be provided, as well as alternatives to those services and services that may be precluded by the grant of the franchise; 
(5)  The willingness and ability of the applicant to meet construction and physical requirements and to abide by all purpose and policy conditions, limitations and requirements with respect to the franchise; and 
(6)  Any other public interest factors or considerations deemed pertinent by the city for safeguarding the interests of the city and the public. 
(Code 2002, § 26-37; Ord. of 5-14-2001(2), § 10-7-7) 
Sec. 30-26. - Procedure for consideration of and action on applications. 
(a)  The city may make such investigations and take or authorize the taking of such other steps as the mayor and council deems necessary or appropriate to consider and act on applications for franchises and determine whether a franchise should be granted to an applicant, and may require the applicant to furnish additional information and data for this purpose. In considering applications, the mayor and council may seek advice from other city officials or bodies, from such other advisory bodies as it may establish or determine appropriate, or from the public, and may request the preparation of one or more reports to be submitted to the mayor and council, which may include recommendations with respect to such applications. 
(b)  If the mayor and council, after considering such information as it determines to be appropriate, elects to further consider one or more applications, the mayor and council shall set one or more public hearings for consideration of the application, fixing and setting forth a day, hour and place certain when and where any persons having any interest therein or objections thereto may file written comments and appear before the mayor and council and be heard, and providing notice of such public hearing in accordance with applicable law. 
(c)  The mayor and council may authorize negotiations between city officials and applicants to determine whether the city and such applicants are able to reach agreement on the terms of the proposed franchise. 
(d)  Upon completion of the steps deemed appropriate by the mayor and council, the mayor and council may grant the franchise, and may specify the conditions under which the franchise is granted. Alternatively, the city may reject any and all applications from whatever source and whenever received except that a franchising authority may not grant an exclusive franchise and may not unreasonably refuse to award an additional competitive franchise. The city also reserves the right to waive any or all requirements when it determines that the best interest of the city may be served thereby and may, if it so desires, request new or additional proposals. 
(Code 2002, § 26-38; Ord. of 5-14-2001(2), § 10-7-8) 
Sec. 30-27. - Terms and conditions of franchise. 
The terms and conditions applicable to any franchise granted pursuant to this article shall be set forth in the separate ordinance granting the franchise or in a separate written agreement. Such separate ordinance or written agreement, among other things, shall address the following subjects: 
(1)  The term of the franchise; 
(2)  The franchise area and the cable services and other telecommunications services and purposes of such other telecommunications services, if any, which are the subject of the franchise; 
(3)  The compensation to be paid to the city, which may include the payment of fees or the provision of facilities or services, or both; 
(4)  The circumstances upon which the franchise may be terminated or cancelled; 
(5)  The mechanisms, such as performance bonds, security funds or letters of credit, to be put in place to ensure the performance of the franchisee's obligations under the franchise; 
(6)  The city's right to inspect the facilities and records of the franchisee; 
(7)  Insurance and indemnification requirements applicable to the franchisee; 
(8)  The obligation of the franchisee to maintain complete and accurate books of account and records, and the city's inspection rights with respect thereto; 
(9)  Provisions to ensure quality workmanship and construction methods; 
(10)  Provisions to ensure that the franchisee will comply with all applicable city, state and federal laws, regulations, rules and policies including, without limitation, those related to employment, purchasing and investigations; 
(11)  Provisions to ensure adequate oversight and regulation of the franchisee by the city; 
(12)  Provisions to restrict the assignment or other transfer of the franchise without the prior written consent of the city; 
(13)  Remedies available to the city to protect the city's interest in the event of the franchisee's failure to comply with terms and conditions of the franchise; 
(14)  Provisions to ensure that the franchisee will obtain all necessary licenses and permits from, and comply with, all laws, regulations, rules and policies of any governmental body having jurisdiction over the franchisee, including the Federal Communications Commission; 
(15)  Provisions to ensure that the franchisee will protect the property of the city and the delivery of public services from damage or interruption of operations resulting from the construction, operation, maintenance, repair or removal of improvements related to the franchise; 
(16)  Provisions designed to minimize the extent to which the public use of the streets of the city are disrupted in connection with the construction of improvements relating to the franchise; and 
(17)  Such other provisions as the city determines are necessary or appropriate in furtherance of the public interest. 
(Code 2002, § 26-39; Ord. of 5-14-2001(2), § 10-7-9) 
Sec. 30-28. - Delegation. 
Consistent with applicable law, the mayor and council shall have the right to delegate and redelegate, and to revoke any such delegation or redelegation, from time to time, any of its rights or obligations under this article to any body, organization or official. Any such delegation, redelegation or revocation, no matter how often made, shall not be deemed an amendment to this article or to require the consent of any applicant for a franchise or franchisee. The mayor and council may also establish and appoint one or more advisor boards, with such duration and such number of members as the mayor and council shall determine, to advise it on such of the matters which are the subject of this article. 
(Code 2002, § 26-40; Ord. of 5-14-2001(2), § 10-7-11) 
Sec. 30-29. - Retroactive application of article provisions. 
This article shall not be retroactively applied to franchises for cable services and other telecommunications services existing on the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived. 
(Code 2002, § 26-41; Ord. of 5-14-2001(2), § 10-7-12) 
Sec. 30-30. - Franchise fee for state issued cable or video franchise. 
The city hereby requires a franchise fee of five percent of gross revenues generated within the city for any cable or video state franchise issued in its corporate boundaries by the state. 
(Ord. of 2-11-2008, § 1(26-42)) 
Sec. 30-31. - Authorized designee. 
The city hereby authorizes the mayor, upon receipt of notice to the city, of its right to designate a franchise fee for an applicant for or holder of an existing state franchise, to provide written notice to the secretary of state and each applicant for or holder of a state franchise within a service area that is wholly or partially located within the city limits of the five percent franchise fee rate applicable to such applicant or holder of a state franchise. 
(Ord. of 2-11-2008, § 2(26-43)) 
Chapter 32 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Uniform Rules of the Road, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-1 et seq.; power of local authorities generally, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 32-1. - Adoption of rules of the road. 
(a)  Unless otherwise specified in this chapter, O.C.G.A. title 40, ch. 6 (O.C.G.A. § 40-6-1 et seq.), as such provisions may be amended from time to time, is adopted as the traffic ordinance for the city, with like effect as if such state law provisions were cited at length in this section. 
(b)  The city clerk shall, for as long as this chapter is in effect, make O.C.G.A. title 40, ch. 6 available for inspection by the public during regular office hours of the city. 
(Code 2002, § 28-1; Ord. of 4-10-2000, §§ 11-101, 11-102) 
Sec. 32-2. - Authority to erect and use traffic signs and signals. 
The chief of police or marshal of the city shall have the authority to erect and use traffic signs and signals in the streets of the city, as directed by the mayor and council. 
(Code 2002, § 28-2; Ord. of 4-10-2000, § 11-401) 
Sec. 32-3. - Compliance with signs and signals; damage or removal. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to fail to comply with the instructions displayed on signs and signals, and it shall be unlawful for any person to damage or remove any such equipment without proper authority from the police department of the city. 
(Code 2002, § 28-3; Ord. of 4-10-2000, § 11-402) 
Sec. 32-4. - Speed limits. 
(a)  On-system. The following speed zones are established for State Highways 41 and 85W, with signs to be erected by the state department of transportation: 
(1)  SR 41. 
a.  From the south city limits (m.p. 5.11) to Main Street (m.p. 5.75), a distance of 0.64 miles, to be zoned for 35 mph. 
b.  From Main Street (m.p. 5.75) to Alt. SR 85 (m.p. 5.91), a distance of 0.16 miles, to be zoned for 25 mph. 
c.  From Alt. SR 85 (m.p. 5.91) to the north city limits (m.p. 6.14), a distance of 0.23 miles, to be zoned for 35 mph. 
(2)  Alt. SR 85. 
a.  From the west city limits (m.p. 3.38) to the CSX Railroad overpass (m.p. 4.00), a distance of 0.67 miles, to be zoned for 35 mph. 
b.  From the CSX Railroad overpass (m.p. 4.00) to the east city limits (m.p. 4.27), a distance of 0.27 miles, to be zoned for 45 mph. 
(3)  Other. Broad Street, from SR 41 to River Road, a distance of 0.39 miles, to be zoned for 25 mph. 
(b)  Off-system. Speed limits on the streets listed in this subsection shall be as indicated, with signs to be erected by the city: 
(1)  Bullock Street, from Oak Street to SR 41, a distance of 0.20 miles, to be zoned for 30 mph. 
(2)  Cold Springs Road, from SR 41 to Alt. SR 85, a distance of 0.36 miles, to be zoned for 25 mph. 
(3)  Cold Springs Road, from Alt. SR 85 to SR 41, a distance of 0.36 miles, to be zoned for 20 mph. 
(4)  Green Street, from River Road to dead end, a distance of 0.35 miles, to be zoned for 30 mph. 
(5)  Main Street, from SR 41 to Fisheries Street, a distance of 0.35 miles, to be zoned for 30 mph. 
(6)  Main Street, from SR 41 to Broad Street, a distance of 0.10 miles, to be zoned for 15 mph. 
(7)  Oak Street, from Broad Street Ext. to Bullock Street, a distance of 0.23 miles, to be zoned for 30 mph. 
(Code 2002, § 28-4; Ord. of 4-10-2000, § 11-202; Ord. of 6-11-2000) 
State Law reference— Alteration of speed limits by local authorities, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-183. 
Secs. 32-5—32-26. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PARKING[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Authority to regulate or prohibit stopping, standing and parking, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371(a)(1); stopping, standing and parking, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-200 et seq. 

Sec. 32-27. - Prohibited at certain places. 
No person shall stand or park a vehicle except when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or with the provisions of this article or in compliance with the directions of a police officer in any of the following places: 
(1)  On a sidewalk. 
(2)  In front of a public or private driveway. 
(3)  Within an intersection. 
(4)  Within five feet of a fire hydrant. 
(5)  In a crosswalk. 
(6)  Alongside or opposite any street excavation or obstruction when such standing or parking would obstruct traffic. 
(7)  Alongside any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or curb of a street. 
(8)  At any place where signs prohibit stopping or standing. 
(9)  Within one foot of another parked vehicle. 
(10)  Upon any street, other than an alley, leaving less than ten feet of the width of the roadway for free movement of vehicular traffic, except that an operator may stop temporarily during the actual loading or unloading of passengers or material. 
(Code 2002, § 28-41; Ord. of 4-10-2000, § 11-501) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-203. 
Sec. 32-28. - Towing of improperly parked vehicles. 
The chief of police, or his designee, may tow any improperly parked vehicle to some convenient storage place, to be redeemed by a fine set by the mayor and council. 
(Code 2002, § 28-42; Ord. of 4-10-2000, § 11-502) 
Sec. 32-29. - Parking in alleys. 
No driver, operator or person having charge of any motor vehicle, shall park the vehicle in or along any alley in the city, except for such time as may be necessary for the purpose of immediately taking on or discharging passengers or freight. 
(Code 2002, § 28-43; Ord. of 4-10-2000, § 11-503) 
Sec. 32-30. - Parking vehicle for sale. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to park any vehicle displayed for sale upon a street. 
(Code 2002, § 28-44; Ord. of 4-10-2000, § 11-504) 
Chapter 34 - UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes:

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 34-1—34-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - WATER AND SEWER SYSTEMS[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Authority to provide stormwater, sewerage collection and disposal systems, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(7); authority to provide for the development storage and distribution of water. Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(7); authority to acquire, construct, extend, operate, maintain and collect fees for water and sewerage systems, O.C.G.A. § 36-34-5. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 34-19. - Application for water and sewer service; deposit required. 
The customer shall make application on the prescribed form for water and sewer service, in person, at the city hall, and at the time the application is made shall make a cash security deposit in the amount determined by the mayor and council. 
(Code 2002, § 30-31; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 2) 
Sec. 34-20. - Administrative fee. 
In addition to the cash deposit in accordance with section 34-19, there shall be paid a nonrefundable administrative fee in the amount determined by the mayor and council. 
(Code 2002, § 30-32; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 3) 
Sec. 34-21. - Tap fees. 
(a)  Persons desiring to connect to the city water and or sewer system shall pay a tap fee in the amount determined by the mayor and council. 
(b)  For any tap which is not of the standard three-fourths-inch, the additional costs will be charged to the customer for the meter and necessary fittings. 
(Code 2002, § 30-33; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 4) 
Sec. 34-22. - Suspension of service. 
(a)  When water and sewer service is discontinued, and all amounts owing are paid, the security deposit shall be refunded to the consumer. 
(b)  Upon discontinuance of service for nonpayment of bills, the security deposit will be applied toward the settlement of the account. Any remaining balance will be refunded to the consumer at his last known address. If the security deposit is insufficient to fully satisfy the account, the city may proceed to collect the balance in the usual way provided by law for collection of debts. 
(c)  Service that has been disconnected for nonpayment will be restored only after payment of all outstanding balances, including the reconnection charge and any additional security deposit that may be required by the mayor and council. 
(d)  The city reserves the right to discontinue service without notice for the following additional reasons: 
(1)  Prevention of fraud or abuse; 
(2)  Consumer's willful disregard for the city's regulations; 
(3)  Emergency repairs; 
(4)  Insufficiency of water supply due to circumstances beyond the city's control; 
(5)  Legal processes; 
(6)  Direction of public authorities; 
(7)  Strike, riot, fire, flood or unavoidable accident. 
(Code 2002, § 30-34; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 11) 
Sec. 34-23. - City's responsibility and liability. 
(a)  The city shall run a service line from its distribution line to the property of the consumer to be served. 
(b)  The city may make connections to service other properties not adjacent to its lines upon payment of reasonable costs for the extension of its water and or sewer lines, as may be required to render such service. 
(c)  The city may install its meter at or near the property line or at the city's option, on the consumer's property within three feet of the property line. 
(d)  The city reserves the right to refuse service unless the consumer's lines or piping are installed in such a manner as to prevent cross connections or backflow. 
(e)  Under normal conditions the consumer will be notified of any anticipated interruptions of service by the city. 
(f)  Water furnished for a given lot shall be used on that lot only and, except for fire protection, the city shall not, under any circumstances, furnish water free of charge to any person, unless approved by the mayor and council. 
(Code 2002, § 30-35; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 5) 
Sec. 34-24. - Consumer's responsibility and liability. 
(a)  Water furnished by the city shall be used for consumption by the consumer, members of his household, guests and employees only. The consumer shall not sell water to any person or permit any other person to use such water. 
(b)  Where a meter or meter box is placed on the premises of the consumer, a suitable place shall be provided by the consumer therefor, unobstructed and accessible at all times to the meter reader. 
(c)  The consumer shall furnish and maintain a private inline cutoff valve on the consumer's side of the meter. 
(d)  The consumer's piping and apparatus shall be installed and maintained by the consumer at the consumer's expense, in a safe and efficient manner, and in accordance with the sanitary regulations of the state health department. 
(e)  To be entitled to receive water from the city's water system, applicants must offer proof that private wells located on their property are not physically connected to the lines of the city's water system. By becoming consumers of the city's system, applicants covenant and agree that, so long as they continue to be consumers of the city system, they will not permit the connection of any private wells on their property to the city's water system. Additionally, the consumer shall not discharge any wastewater to the sewer system that is not generated by potable water furnished by the city. 
(Code 2002, § 30-36; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 6(A)—(E)) 
Sec. 34-25. - Acceptable and unacceptable discharge limits. 
The consumer agrees to limit discharge into the sewage system to that strength of sewage defined by trade usage as domestic sewage. The limitations on acceptable discharge are: 
(1)  Inadmissible. 
a.  The following wastes are strictly inadmissible: 
1.  Wastes which create a fire or explosion hazard in the sewage lines or treatment plant; 
2.  Waste products which will impair the hydraulic capacity of the sewer system; 
3.  Wastes which, in any quantity, create a hazard to people, the sewer system, the treatment process or the receiving waters. 
b.  Examples of such inadmissible wastes are as follows: gasoline, fuel line discharge, cleaning solvents and paint vehicles; ashes, sand, cinders, metal, broken glass, wood and metal shavings, rags and unshredded garbage; and hydrogen sulfide, sulfur dioxide, cyanides, acids and caustics. 
(2)  Maximum temperature. The maximum permissible temperature of any discharge shall be 150 degrees Fahrenheit (65 degrees Celsius). 
(3)  Oils, fats and grease. Volatile oils shall not be allowed in any amount. Mineral oil shall be removed to the maximum degree practical before discharge. Vegetable oils, fats and grease shall be limited to no more than 15 milligrams per liter (mg/l). Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be installed where food is prepared or served for public consumption and or sale. 
a.  Interceptors are necessary for the proper handling of liquid wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand or other harmful ingredients. Such interceptors shall not be required for private living quarters or dwelling units. 
b.  All interceptors shall be of a type and with the capacity to handle excessive amounts of grease, oil and sand. 
c.  Interceptors shall be located so as to be readily and easily accessible for regular and timely cleaning and inspection. 
d.  Interceptors shall be supplied, and properly maintained in satisfactory and effective operation, by the owner at his expense. 
e.  All eating and/or drinking establishments, ice cream parlors, schools, churches, hospitals, nursing homes, hotels, motels, and bed and breakfasts shall be in compliance with this article before an occupational tax certificate can be issued. 
f.  Establishment not in compliance with this article shall be in violation punishable as set forth in the city Charter. 
(4)  pH. The pH of influent waste shall be between 5.5 and 9.5. 
(5)  Acceptable discharges. 
a.  Substances toxic to biological wastewater treatment processes such as copper, chromium, lead, zinc, arsenic and nickel may also be limited if such substances are present in sufficient quantity to adversely affect treatment. Acceptable amounts of such substances are as follows, unless otherwise determined by independent study and accepted by the city: 
1.  Nickel: Equal to or less than five mg/l. 
2.  Zinc: Equal to or less than ten mg/l. 
3.  Chromium (+3): Equal to or less than ten mg/l. 
4.  Chromium (+6): Equal to or less than 0.05 mg/l. 
5.  Chlorine residual: Equal to or less than 0.5 mg/l. 
6.  Cyanides: None allowed. 
7.  Cyanates: None allowed. 
8.  Isocyanates: None allowed. 
b.  All others: None allowed without an independent justifying study and tests accepted by the city. 
(6)  BOD. The maximum allowable five-day biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) that will be accepted without surcharge payments shall be 250 milligrams per liter (mg/l). 
(7)  Suspended solids. The maximum allowable amount of suspended solids that will be accepted without surcharge payments shall be 250 mg/l. 
(Code 2002, § 30-37; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 6(F)) 
Sec. 34-26. - Surcharge assessments. 
(a)  Users of the city's wastewater system may be subject to annual sampling of their wastewater discharge at the discretion of the mayor and council. The purpose of such sampling shall be to determine if the user is in compliance with the terms of this article. Contributors to the system will be charged for any BOD and suspended solids which exceed the limits of section 34-25. 
(b)  Monthly surcharge billings shall be based on the amount of water used. BOD and suspended solids which exceed the limits of section 34-25 are computed as follows: 
(1)  BOD (in mg/l) times 8.34 times water consumption times $0.12. 
(2)  Suspended solids (in mg/l) times 8.34 times water consumption times $0.12. 
(3)  Where water consumption is expressed in millions of gallons. 
(4)  Wastewater sampling results shall be used as a basis for the surcharge for not more than 12 months. 
(Code 2002, § 30-38; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 7) 
Sec. 34-27. - Access to premises and extensions of system. 
(a)  Duly authorized agents of the city shall have access at all hours to the premises of the consumer for the purpose of installing or removing city property, inspecting piping, reading and testing meters, or for any other purpose in connection with the water and sewer services and their facilities. 
(b)  Extensions to the systems shall be made only when the consumer shall grant or convey, or shall cause to be granted or conveyed, to the city a permanent easement of right-of-way across any property traversed by the water or sewer lines. 
(Code 2002, § 30-39; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 8) 
Sec. 34-28. - Change of occupancy. 
Not less than three days' notice must be given, in person or in writing, at the city hall to discontinue water and sewer service or to change occupancy. The outgoing party shall be responsible for all water consumed up to the time of departure, or the time specified for departure, whichever period is longer. The new occupant shall apply for water service within 48 hours after occupying the premises. Failure to do so will make him liable for payment for the water consumed since the last meter reading. 
(Code 2002, § 30-40; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 9) 
Secs. 34-29—34-59. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - RATES AND CHARGES; BILLING AND COLLECTION 

Sec. 34-60. - Rate schedule. 
The water and sewer rates, meter rates included, shall be as determined from time to time by the mayor and council. 
(Code 2002, § 30-61; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 1; Ord. of 12-11-2000, § 1) 
Sec. 34-61. - Meter reading; billing; collections. 
Bills to customers for water and sewer service shall be mailed on such days each month as may be determined by the city. Failure of water and/or sewer users to pay charges duly imposed shall result in the automatic imposition of the following penalties: 
(1)  Nonpayment by the due date shown on the bill will be subject to a penalty of ten percent of the delinquent account. 
(2)  Nonpayment within ten days from the due date will result in the water being shut off from the water user's property. All charges, current and past due, including additional charges and fees, must be paid in full before the consumer's water meter will be reconnected. A reconnection charge as established from time to time by the mayor and council shall be imposed. 
(3)  Failure to make payment within 60 days of the original billing date will allow the city, in addition to all other rights and remedies, to terminate service. In such event, the consumer shall not be entitled to receive, nor the city obligated to supply, any water under this agreement. 
(4)  The owners of vacant or unoccupied property may continue to receive water and sewer service. However, meter and usage charges must continue to be paid. Once service is terminated, a new user or owner of vacant or unoccupied property shall be treated as new users, and shall apply for service and pay fees and deposits as per sections 34-20 and 34-21. 
(5)  Bills shall be paid, in person or by mail, at the city hall. Failure to receive bills or notices shall not prevent such bills from becoming delinquent, nor relieve the consumer from payment of such bills. 
(6)  Partial payments will not be accepted at any time. Disputed bills shall be paid in full, and a request for adjustment may be filed with the city clerk for consideration by the mayor and council at the next meeting following receipt of such request. 
(Code 2002, § 30-62; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 10) 
Sec. 34-62. - Complaints; adjustments. 
(a)  If a consumer believes his bill to be in error, he shall present his claim, in person, at the city hall before the bill becomes delinquent. Such claim, if made after the bill has become delinquent, shall not prevent discontinuance of service as provided in section 34-61. The consumer may pay such bill under protest, and such payment shall not prejudice his claim. 
(b)  The city will make a special water meter reading at the request of a consumer for a fee as established from time to time by the mayor and council; provided, however, that if such special reading discloses that the meter was misread, no charge will be made. 
(c)  Water meters will be tested at the request of the consumer upon payment to the city of the actual costs of conducting the test, but not less than an amount as established from time to time by the mayor and council. No charge will be made, however, if the meter is found to over register beyond three percent of the correct volume. 
(d)  If the seal of a meter is broken by other than the city's representative, or if the meter fails to register correctly or is stopped for any cause, the consumer shall pay an amount estimated from the record of his previous bills and/or from other proper data. 
(Code 2002, § 30-63; Ord. of 1-10-2000(1), § 12) 
Secs. 34-63—34-82. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - DROUGHT CONTINGENCY PLAN 

Sec. 34-83. - General requirements. 
(a)  Introduction. 
(1)  Safe and high quality drinking water is a precious resource in the state and the city. This drought contingency and water emergency plan (the "plan") requires that the available water treatment and storage resources of the city water plant be put to maximum beneficial use along with the available water resources and storage of the city to the maximum extent possible. 
(2)  The plan also requires that the waste or unreasonable use, or unreasonable method of use of water be prevented, and the conservation of water be extended with a view to reasonable and beneficial use in the interests of the people of the city and for the public health and welfare. This is especially true during times of drought or emergency. Emergency conditions resulting from equipment or system failures are also addressed in this plan. 
(b)  Coordination. 
(1)  This plan has been coordinated with the mayor, the city council, the chief of police, the water plant superintendent, and interested citizens. 
(2)  The plan will be reviewed and updated as necessary at a minimum of every two years. The plan is subject to the requirement that at least one public hearing be held. 
(c)  Authorization. The mayor on behalf of the city council is hereby authorized and directed to implement the applicable provisions of this plan upon determination that such implementation is necessary to protect public health, safety, and welfare of the citizens of the city. The mayor shall have the authority to initiate or terminate drought stages or water supply emergency response measures as described in this plan. 
(d)  Public education. The city will periodically provide the public with information about the plan including information about the conditions under which each stage of the plan is to be increased, reduced or terminated and the drought response measures to be implemented in each stage. This information will be provided by means of press releases, public service announcements, utility bill inserts, public events, and similar methods. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2010, § 30-75) 
Sec. 34-84. - Application. 
(a)  The provisions of this plan shall apply to all customers of the city. Utilization of a water source other than city potable water is exempt from the provisions of this plan. Daily water demand will be monitored for drought and emergency conditions by the city. Trigger conditions under this plan will be based on reductions in flow from the cold spring, a lack of treatment capacity, an emergency situation caused by a natural disaster, equipment or system failure, or high daily average water demand. 
(b)  The mayor, on recommendation of city water plant operator, shall determine when conditions warrant initiation or termination of each stage of the plan. 
(c)  The trigger conditions described below are based on the fact that the city uses water from the cold spring under a proposed state issued withdrawal permit as its water supply. Importantly, the city has contractual agreements whereby the U.S. Fish Hatchery is entitled to two-thirds of the water which can be produced by the cold spring which will not be impacted. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2010, § 30-76) 
Sec. 34-85. - Trigger conditions. 
(a)  Monitoring of water demand. Daily water demand will be monitored for emergency conditions by the city water plant operator and water plant employees. Trigger conditions will be based on emergency situations caused by drought conditions, a natural disaster, equipment or system failure, or high daily average water demand. The mayor, on the recommendation of the water plant operator, shall determine when conditions warrant initiation or termination of each state of the plan. 
(1)  Stage 1; standard water conservation. 
a.  Customers may be required to conserve water on an ongoing basis as the standard for the city. Customers must adhere to water restrictions on nonessential water use, as outlined herein in responses to trigger conditions, stage 1; standard water conservation. 
b.  These water restrictions are adopted as the standard operating procedure for nonessential water usage on a year round basis. 
(2)  Stage 2; high water demand. 
a.  Requirement for initiation. Customers shall be required to comply with the requirements and restrictions on nonessential water uses, as outlined herein in responses to trigger conditions, stage 2, when average daily water production at the city water plant exceeds 300,000 gallons (0.30 mil gal) per day for five consecutive days. 
b.  Requirements for termination. Stage 2 of the plan may be rescinded by the mayor when the condition listed above as triggering events have ceased to exist for a period of five consecutive days. 
c.  Resumption of previous stage. Upon termination of stage 2, stage 1 becomes operative. 
(3)  Stage 3; severe water shortage. 
a.  Requirements. Customers shall be required to comply with the requirements and restriction on nonessential water uses, as outlined herein in responses to trigger conditions, stage 3, when average daily water production at the city water plant exceeds 300,000 gallons (0.35 mil gals) per day for five consecutive days. 
b.  Requirements for termination. Stage 3 of the plan may be rescinded by the mayor when the condition listed above as triggering events have ceased to exist for a period of three consecutive days. Upon termination of stage 3, stage 2 becomes operative as directed by the mayor. 
(4)  Stage 4; water supply emergency. 
a.  Requirements for initiation. Customer shall be required to comply with the requirements and restrictions on nonessential water uses, as outlined herein in responses to trigger conditions, stage 4, when: 
1.  Average daily water production at the city water plant exceeds 375,000 gallons (0.375 mil gals) per day for five consecutive days; 
2.  The city water system is contaminated whether accidentally or intentionally. A water supply emergency condition is reached immediately upon detection; or 
3.  The city water system fails for any reason. A water supply emergency condition is reached immediately upon detection. 
b.  Requirement for termination. Stage 4 of the plan may be rescinded by the mayor when the condition listed above as triggering events have ceased to exist. Upon termination of stage 4, the previously initiated stage becomes operative as directed by the mayor. 
(b)  Notification. 
(1)  Public meeting. This plan will be presented to the public at a formal public meeting of the city council. 
(2)  Publication. Public notification of the initiation or termination of drought response stages shall be by means of publication in the legal organ, in a newspaper widely circulated in the city and/or by public service announcements on local radio, television and/or cable service. Additional methods of public notification may include signs posted in public places, utility bill inserts, and other means to be determined by the city. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2010, § 30-77) 
Sec. 34-86. - Responses to trigger conditions. 
The city shall monitor water supply and/or demand conditions on a daily basis and, in accordance the triggering criteria set forth herein, shall determine that a voluntary, moderate or severe shortage condition exists and shall implement the following actions upon notice as provided herein: 
(1)  Stage 1; standard water conservation. 
a.  Generally. The goal for stage 1 of the plan is to raise public and customer awareness of water demand, conditions, and water conservation and to limit the nonessential use of outdoor water especially as it relates to watering of lawns, plants and flowers. 
b.  Standard water use restrictions. Water customers are required to limit nonessential residential and commercial water use by practicing water conservation year round and reducing nonessential water uses, as follows: 
1.  Standard outdoor watering restrictions. 
(i)  Odd-numbered addresses may water only on Tuesdays, Thursdays and Sundays. Watering is allowed only between the hours of 10:00 p.m. until 10:00 a.m. and only for a period not to exceed 30 minutes per watering. 
(ii)  Even-numbered addresses may water only on Mondays, Wednesdays and Saturdays. Watering is allowed only between the hours of 10:00 p.m. until 10:00 a.m. and only for a period not to exceed 30 minutes per watering. 
(iii)  No outdoor watering on Fridays. 
2.  Low flow devices required. Beginning January 1, 2010, the city shall require the installation of low flow water devices in all new construction and/or renovation within the city limits; specifically, but not limited to, toilets, faucets, and showerheads. Such low flow devices shall be required as a condition under any building permit issued with the city limits. 
(2)  Stage 2; high water demand. 
a.  Generally. The goal for stage 2 of the plan is to reduce and maintain average daily water production at or below 300,000 gallons (0.30 mil gals) per day. 
b.  Standard water use restrictions. In the event that the mayor enacts stage 2, the following water use restrictions shall apply to all persons: All water customers are required to participate in the two day per week watering schedule for nonessential water use. Nonessential water use shall only occur on the designated outdoor watering days. The initial two-day watering schedule shall be as follows unless adjusted by resolution of the city council: 
1.  Odd-numbered addresses may water only on either Tuesdays or Thursdays, but not both days, during each week. Watering is allowed only between the hours of 10:00 p.m. until 10:00 a.m., and only for a period not to exceed 30 minutes. 
2.  Even-numbered addresses may water only on either Mondays or Wednesdays but not both days during each week. Watering is allowed only between the hours of 10:00 p.m. until 10:00 a.m., and only for a period not to exceed 30 minutes. 
3.  No outdoor watering on Fridays, Saturdays or Sundays. 
(i)  Nonessential water use is permitted under subsection (2)b.1 of this section with the following restrictions: The use of hand-held hoses equipped with a positive pistol grip nozzle or other device that automatically shuts off water flow when the hose is not being held by the water user, by drip irrigation, by soaker hose, or by handheld buckets. 
(ii)  Subsection (2)b.1 of this section time restrictions do not apply to: 
A.  The irrigation of commercial plant nurseries. 
B.  Irrigation using reclaimed water. 
C.  New landscape installation during planting and the first ten days after planting. 
D.  The testing of new irrigation systems or existing irrigation systems being tested or under repair. 
(iii)  The washing of individual automobiles, trucks, motorbikes, boats, trailers, airplanes or other vehicles is not permitted. 
(iv)  The washing of individual vehicles may be done at any time on the immediate premises of a commercial car wash or commercial service station. 
(v)  This restriction does not apply to the washing of vehicles or any other type of mobile equipment (such as garbage trucks and vehicles to transport food and perishables) when the health, safety, and welfare of the public is contingent upon frequent vehicle cleansing. 
(vi)  Charity car washes are prohibited. 
(vii)  Use of water to fill, refill, or add to any indoor or outdoor swimming pools, wading pools, or Jacuzzi-type pools is permitted only on designated watering days as provided under stage 2, subsection 2(b) of this section. 
(viii)  Operation of any ornamental fountain or pond for aesthetic or scenic purposes is prohibited except where necessary to support aquatic life. This restriction does not apply to ornamental fountains or ponds that use reclaimed water, non-potable water, or water sources other than the city water supply. 
(ix)  Use of water from fire hydrants shall be limited to firefighting and related activities, or other activities necessary to maintain public health, safety, and welfare. Use of water from designated fire hydrants for construction purposes may be allowed when a variance has been approved by the mayor. 
(x)  Use of water for the irrigation of golf course greens, tees, and fairways is permitted only on designated watering days. These restrictions do not apply to the irrigation of any golf course that uses reclaimed water, or other non-potable water sources. 
(xi)  All restaurants are prohibited from serving water to their patrons except when requested. 
(xii)  The following uses constitute a waste of water and are prohibited: 
A.  Noncommercial pressure washing; 
B.  Washing sidewalks, walkways, driveways, parking lots, tennis courts, patios or other hard-surfaced areas except to alleviate immediate health or safety hazards. 
C.  Use of water for dust control. 
D.  Allowing water to run off a property or allowing water to pond in the street or parking lot. 
E.  Operating an irrigation system with sprinkler heads that are broken or out of adjustment. 
F.  Failure to repair a controllable leak within a reasonable period after having been given notice directing the repair of such leak. 
G.  Washing an automobile, truck, trailer, boat, airplane, or other mobile equipment with a hand-held hose not equipped with a pistol grip nozzle or other device that automatically shuts off water flow when the hose is not being held by the water user. 
(3)  Stage 3; severe water shortage. 
a.  Generally. The goal for stage 3 of the plan is to reduce and maintain average daily water demand at or below 350,000 gallons (0.35 mil gals) per day. 
b.  Standard water use restrictions. In the event that the mayor enacts stage 3, the following water use restrictions shall apply to all persons: 
1.  Supply management measures. The city will cease the flushing of water mains except when necessary to maintain public health, safety, and welfare. All city departments will discontinue irrigating public landscaped areas except when such areas are irrigated with reclaimed water, or water sources other than that provided by the city. 
2.  Additional water use restrictions. All requirements of stage 2 shall remain in effect during stage 3, with these additional water use restrictions: 
(i)  No outdoor watering for lawns, plants, and gardens shall be allowed. 
(ii)  Nonessential water use is restricted to use of hand-held buckets, or hand-held hoses equipped with a positive pistol grip nozzle, or other device that automatically shuts off water flow when the hose is not being held by the water user. 
(iii)  No pressure washing of homes or buildings shall be allowed. 
(iv)  The washing of automobiles, trucks, trailers, boats, airplanes, and other types of mobile equipment not occurring on the immediate premises of a commercial car wash or a commercial service station and not in the immediate interest of the public health, safety, and welfare are prohibited. 
(v)  Commercial plant nurseries may use only hand-held buckets, or handheld hoses equipped with a positive pistol grip nozzle, or other device that automatically shuts off water flow when the hose is not being held by the water user. 
(vi)  The filling, refilling, or adding of potable water to ornamental fountains, decorative fountains or pools, swimming or wading pools is prohibited. 
(vii)  No new landscapes of any type may be installed. 
(viii)  All variances granted under a previous stage shall be invalid during stage 3. The use of water under variances granted by the mayor is to be discontinued. 
(4)  Stage 4; water supply emergency. The goal for stage 4, water supply emergency, is to rectify the emergency and return to normal operating conditions as soon as possible. In the event of an imminent or actual water supply emergency due to either loss of water supply sources (including contamination) and/or system failure, the mayor has the authority to initiate the following water supply emergency responses: 
a.  Effective immediately upon initiation of stage 4, all nonessential water use shall be discontinued, except for immediate health and safety purposes. 
b.  In the event that water shortage or water emergency conditions threaten public health, safety, and welfare, the mayor, upon recommendation of city water plant operator, may order water rationing and/or terminate service to selected users of the system in accordance with the following sequence: 
1.  Recreational users; 
2.  Commercial users; 
3.  Residential users; 
4.  School users; and 
5.  Hospitals, public health, and safety facilities. 
c.  Prior to the termination of any service to any user, the mayor shall first attempt to ration water usage. Such rationing does not have to be uniform or pro rata between any of the classifications of subsection (3) of this section. 
d.  Public notification of stage 4 conditions. In the event that minimum health and safety standards for drinking water are not met during emergency conditions, public service announcements on local television and radio stations will be utilized to notify the public of the emergency conditions and response measures. These response measures may include notifying the public of the need to boil water, use bottled water, or use a designated alternate water source, as appropriate. 
e.  Emergency management assistance. If necessary, the mayor on behalf of the city may seek assistance through the local and/or state emergency management programs. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2010, § 30-78) 
Sec. 34-87. - Variances. 
(a)  The mayor may, in writing, grant a temporary variance for existing water uses otherwise prohibited under this plan if it is determined that failure to grant such a variance would cause an emergency condition adversely affecting the health, sanitation, or fire protection for the public or the person requesting such variances, or if one or more of the following conditions are met: 
(1)  Compliance with this plan cannot be technically accomplished during the duration of the water supply shortage or other condition for which the plan is in effect. 
(2)  Alternative methods can be implemented which will achieve the same level of reduction in water use. 
(b)  Persons requesting an exemption from the provisions of this ordinance shall file a petition for variance with the city. All petitions for variances shall be reviewed by the mayor and shall include the following: 
(1)  Name and address of the petitioner; 
(2)  Purpose of water use; 
(3)  Specific provision of the plan from which the petitioner is requesting relief; 
(4)  Detailed statements as to how the specific provision of the plan adversely affects the petitioner or what damage or harm will occur to the petitioner or others if the petitioner complies with this plan; 
(5)  Description of the relief requested; 
(6)  Period of time for which the variance is sought; 
(7)  Alternative water use restrictions or other measures the petitioner is taking or proposes to take to meet the intent of this plan and the compliance date; 
(8)  Estimated water savings, as a percentage of normal monthly water use, while operating under the variance requested; and 
(9)  Other information requested by the city. 
(c)  Variances granted by the mayor shall be subject to the following conditions, unless waived or modified: 
(1)  Variances granted shall include a timetable for compliance. 
(2)  Variances granted in a particular stage shall expire upon advancing to a more restrictive stage of the plan. 
(3)  Petitioners shall prominently display the variance granted where it can be read by the general public at all location for which the variance applies, and make said variance available to the public. 
(4)  Variances granted may be revoked by the mayor if the petitioner fails to meet specific requirements set forth in the variance. 
(d)  No variance shall be retroactive or otherwise justify any violation of this plan occurring prior to the issuance of the variance. 
(e)  No variance may be granted as to a stage 4, water supply emergency. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2010, § 30-79) 
Sec. 34-88. - Wholesale agreements/contracts provision. 
In the event that the trigger conditions specified by stage 3, severe water shortage, or stage 4, water supply emergency, of this plan are met and a stage 3 or stage 4 condition declared by the mayor is hereby authorized to initiate allocation of water supplies to wholesale customers on a pro rata basis. This stipulation applies to all existing and future wholesale water supply contracts or agreements made with the city. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2010, § 30-80) 
Sec. 34-89. - Enforcement. 
(a)  In addition to any fines provided for by local ordinance, no person shall allow potable water from the city to be used for residential, commercial, industrial, agricultural, governmental, or any other purpose in a manner contrary to any provision of this plan, or in an amount in excess of that permitted by the stage in effect at the time pursuant to action taken by the mayor in accordance with provisions of this plan. 
(b)  If a person should have two or more distinct violations of this plan, the city shall provide written notice to the person of proposed termination of service. The notice shall apprise the person of a date for termination of service, the reasons for such termination, and afford the person an opportunity to present his objections to termination in a hearing before the city council. 
(c)  The person shall have not less than ten days to present his objections in writing to the mayor and the city council. 
(d)  If, after hearing, the city council determines that service will be terminated; such termination shall take place within five business days. Services discontinued pursuant to this plan and/or by local ordinance shall be restored only upon payment of the re-connection charge in the amount of $200.00 and any other costs incurred by the city in discontinuing or reconnecting service. 
(e)  In addition, suitable assurance must be given to the mayor, that the same action shall not be repeated while the plan is in effect. Anyone who after disconnection pursuant to this plan and later re-connection may be permanently prohibited from receiving water service or may be required to post a bond in an amount satisfactory to the city council in order to receive future city water service. 
(f)  Compliance with this plan may also be sought through injunctive relief in the superior court. In such event, if the city is upheld, the customer shall pay attorney's fees and costs. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2010, § 30-81) 
Sec. 34-90. - Presumptions. 
(a)  Any person, in apparent control of the property where a violation occurs or originates, shall be presumed to be the violator, and proof that the violation occurred on the person's property shall constitute a rebuttable presumption that the person in apparent control of the property committed the violation, but any such person shall have the right to show that he did not commit the violation. 
(b)  Parents shall be presumed to be responsible for violations of their minor children and proof that a violation, committed by a child, occurred on property within the parents' control shall constitute a rebuttable presumption that the parent committed the violation. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2010, § 30-82) 
Secs. 34-91—34-108. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - TREATMENT OF ADDRESS DISCREPANCIES 

Sec. 34-109. - Purpose. 
Pursuant to 16 CFR 681.1, the purpose of this article is to establish a process by which the city will be able to form a reasonable belief that a consumer report relates to the consumer about whom it has requested a consumer credit report when the city has received a notice of address discrepancy. 
(Ord. No. 09-01, § 2(41-2), 9-14-2009) 
Sec. 34-110. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Notice of address discrepancy means a notice sent to a user by a consumer reporting agency, pursuant to 15 USC 1681(c)(h)(1), that informs the user of a substantial difference between the address for the consumer that the user provided to request the consumer report and the address in the agency's file for the consumer. 
(Ord. No. 09-01, § 2(41-3), 9-14-2009) 
Sec. 34-111. - Policy. 
In the event that the city receives a notice of address discrepancy, the city employee responsible for verifying consumer addresses for the purpose of providing the municipal service or account sought by the consumer shall perform one or more of the following activities, as determined to be appropriate by such employee: 
(1)  Compare the information in the consumer report with: 
a.  Information the city obtains and uses to verify a consumer's identity in accordance with the requirements of the customer information program rules implementing 31 USC 5318(1); 
b.  Information the city maintains in its own records, such as applications for service, change of address notices, other customer account records or tax records; or 
c.  Information the city obtains from third-party sources that are deemed reliable by the relevant city employee; or 
(2)  Verify the information in the consumer report with the consumer. 
(Ord. No. 09-01, § 2(41-4), 9-14-2009) 
Sec. 34-112. - Furnishing consumer's address to consumer reporting agency. 
(a)  In the event that the city reasonably confirms that an address provided by a consumer to the city is accurate, the city is required to provide such address to the consumer reporting agency from which the city received a notice of address discrepancy with respect to such consumer. This information is required to be provided to the consumer reporting agency when: 
(1)  The city is able to form a reasonable belief that the consumer report relates to the consumer about whom the city requested the report; 
(2)  The city establishes a continuing relation with the consumer; and 
(3)  The city regularly and in the ordinary course of business provides information to the consumer reporting agency from which it received the notice of address discrepancy. 
(b)  Such information shall be provided to the consumer reporting agency as part of the information regularly provide by the city to such agency for the reporting period in which the city establishes a relationship with the customer. 
(Ord. No. 09-01, § 2(41-5), 9-14-2009) 
Sec. 34-113. - Methods of confirming consumer addresses. 
The city employee charged with confirming consumer addresses may, in his discretion, confirm the accuracy of an address through one or more of the following methods: 
(1)  Verifying the address with the consumer; 
(2)  Reviewing the city's records to verify the consumer's address; 
(3)  Verifying the address through third-party sources; or 
(4)  Using other reasonable processes. 
(Ord. No. 09-01, § 2(41-6), 9-14-2009) 
Chapter 36 - VEHICLES FOR HIRE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Reciprocal agreements as to operation of vehicles registered in other states inapplicable to motor vehicles for hire, O.C.G.A. § 40-2-95. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 36-1—36-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - HORSE-DRAWN CARRIAGES 

Sec. 36-19. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Company means the holder of a license to operate a horse-drawn carriage business under the provisions of this article whether a person, firm, partnership or corporation. 
Driver means any person who drives or operates a horse-drawn carriage on the streets of the city for a licensed company. 
Driver's permit means the written authority granted by the city for an individual to drive or operate a horse-drawn carriage within the city. 
Horse-drawn carriage means any hack or carriage which is operated by being drawn by a horse, mule or other beast of burden, for the transportation for hire of passengers. 
Inspector (chief of police or his designee) means the individual employee or organizational unit of the city charged with the responsibility for enforcing this article, except for specific responsibilities otherwise provided in this article. 
License means the right and privilege granted by the city for the operation of a business incorporating the use of one or more horse-drawn carriages within the corporate limits of the city. 
Stand means a public place alongside the curb of a street or elsewhere which has been designated by the mayor as reserved exclusively for the use of horse-drawn carriages. 
(Code 2002, § 32-31; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-1) 
Sec. 36-20. - Penalty for violation of article. 
Violation of this article may be grounds for immediate suspension or revocation of the license issued under this article. Penalties for violation of this article are as follows: 
(1)  First offense, a fine of $100.00. 
(2)  Second offense, a fine of $500.00. 
(3)  Third offense, license revoked. 
(Code 2002, § 32-32) 
Sec. 36-21. - Licensing of horse-drawn carriage companies. 
(a)  License. 
(1)  Required. No person shall operate a business involving the use of one or more horse-drawn carriages on the streets of the city unless a license for such business has first been granted by the city. The license shall be effective only for the calendar year stated in the license, unless suspended or revoked sooner as provided by ordinance. The annual license fee shall be as established from time to time by the mayor and council. 
(2)  Application. Application for the license shall be made on forms provided by the city clerk and shall provide such information as is required for other business license applications, and such additional information as may be necessary to define completely the business operation. 
(3)  Certification of EIA. Each applicant must produce, if demanded by the mayor or city clerk, a valid equine infectious anemia (EIA) certification. 
(b)  Operating regulations. In addition to the license requirements imposed in this section, no license shall be issued to any carriage operator unless the operator complies with the following operating regulations: 
(1)  A licensed veterinarian shall certify, after due and proper inspection, the good health of each draft animal before it is placed into service. One such health inspection shall be required for each animal within six months of the application for a license. The inspector may require reexamination of any animal upon appearance of any adverse condition of the animal. 
(2)  No single animal shall pull a carriage holding more than ten people, including the driver. 
(3)  Unless written approval is given by a licensed veterinarian, no animal having open sores or wounds or any disease or ailment shall be permitted to be in service on the streets of the city. 
(4)  Each draft animal shall have its hooves properly trimmed and shod for street surfaces. 
(5)  Each animal shall be groomed daily and not have fungus, dandruff, or a dirty coat. 
(6)  Harnesses shall be properly fitted, maintained, and oiled so that no irritating material will come in direct contact with the animal. 
(7)  No driver may use more than a light touch of the whip upon any animal, and no driver or other persons may forcefully strike an animal, and make movements or noise intended to frighten or harm an animal. 
(8)  No driver shall permit an animal to pull a carriage at a speed faster than a slow trot, except in extreme emergency situations. 
(9)  No animal shall be subject to any condition or treatment, whether in service or out of service, which will impair the good health and physical condition of that animal. 
(10)  Adequate water shall be provided. 
(11)  Ventilation adequate to ensure the health and comfort of animals shall be provided. 
(12)  Food shall be free of contamination. 
(13)  All laws as cited as the Humane Care for Equines Act (O.C.G.A. § 4-13-1 et seq.), as well as all other state and federal laws governing equines. 
(14)  No one animal may be worked more than eight hours per day. The driver must keep a log of the starting and ending times for each animal. Such log should be kept in a bound book form and stored on the carriage being pulled. 
(15)  No driver shall work an animal pulling a horse-drawn carriage when the outside temperature exceeds 95 degrees Fahrenheit. 
(c)  Inspection of operating practices. The inspector shall be empowered to inspect all operating practices of any carriage company to ensure continuous compliance with this article. 
(d)  Failure to comply with article provisions; nonissuance. Any applicant who refuses or fails to comply with the requirements of this article shall not be issued a business license until proof of compliance is presented by the applicant and certified by the inspector. The licensing requirements of this section shall be ongoing as requirements for continuous operation. 
(e)  Suspension. The city clerk may, upon recommendation of the inspector, temporarily suspend any carriage company license for violation of the provisions of this article, subject to license revocation action. 
(Code 2002, § 32-33; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-2) 
Sec. 36-22. - Insurance. 
(a)  Indemnity for benefit of city. Any horse-drawn carriage company operating under this article shall hold the city, its officers, agents, servants and employees, harmless against any and all liability, loss, damages or expense which may accrue to the city by reason of negligence, default or misconduct of the company in connection with the rights granted to such company under this article. Nothing in this article shall be considered to make the city, its officers, agents, servants or employees liable for damages because of any negligent act or omission or commission by any horse-drawn carriage company, its servants, agents, drivers or other employees, during the operation by the company of a horse-drawn carriage business or service, either in respect to injury to persons or with respect to damage to property which may be sustained. 
(b)  Insurance for benefit of passengers. Any horse-drawn carriage company desiring a license to do business shall give and maintain a policy of indemnity from an insurance company authorized to do business in the state for each vehicle in use as a horse-drawn carriage. The minimum coverage shall be $100,000.00 for bodily injury to any one person, $300,000.00 for injury to more than one person which are sustained in the same accident, and $25,000.00 for property damage resulting from one accident. The indemnity insurance shall inure to the benefit of any person who shall be injured or who shall sustain damage to property caused by the negligence of a horse-drawn carriage company, its servants or agents. 
(c)  Blanket policy. Any company or person operating a horse-drawn carriage in the city shall give a separate policy of indemnity insurance for each separate horse-drawn carriage for hire, except where such company or person actually owns or holds legal title to more than one horse-drawn carriage, in which event such company or person may give one policy of indemnity insurance covering all the horse-drawn carriages actually owned. This latter provision, however, shall not apply to any group of persons separately owning horse-drawn carriages who may be jointly operating or doing business under a licensed horse-drawn carriage name. 
(d)  Notice when voided. Before any policy of insurance required by this article is voided for any cause, nonpayment of premium or otherwise, notice shall be given by the licensee in writing, to the city clerk at least five days before the policy shall take effect. 
(Code 2002, § 32-34; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-3) 
Sec. 36-23. - Driver's permit. 
(a)  Required. No person shall operate a horse-drawn carriage for hire upon the streets of the city, and no person who owns or operates a horse-drawn carriage company shall permit a horse-drawn carriage to be driven, and no horse-drawn carriage operating under a horse-drawn carriage company licensed by the city shall be driven at any time for hire, unless the driver of the horse-drawn carriage shall first have obtained and shall have then in force a horse-drawn carriage driver's permit issued under the provisions of this article. 
(b)  Application. Any person desiring a permit required by this article shall submit an application in writing to the city clerk on a form to be furnished by the city clerk. The application shall be made under oath and shall state the age of the applicant, date of birth, his address, and whether he has been convicted of a violation of any of the laws of the state or of this article or other ordinances of the city, and, if so, when and of what offense, and the sentence of the court. 
(c)  Qualifications of applicant. An applicant for a driver's permit under this article must not be less than 18 years of age, with no physical infirmities which might make the applicant an unsafe or unsatisfactory horse-drawn carriage driver. 
(d)  Fee. Before any permit is granted under this article, a driver's permit fee in the amount established by the mayor and council shall be paid by the applicant. 
(e)  Current state driver's license required. Any person applying for a horse-drawn carriage driver's permit under this article must show that he has a current motor vehicle operator's license issued or approved by the state, and that the license is not under suspension or revocation. 
(f)  Examination of applicant. It shall be the duty of the inspector to examine the applicant, police and traffic record, and other vouchers, and thereafter recommend to the clerk to grant or refuse the permit. In the event of a refusal by the clerk to grant a permit, the applicant shall have the right to enter an appeal to the mayor and council. Such appeal shall be filed in writing to the mayor and council within ten calendar days from the date of refusal to grant the permit. The mayor and council must convene an appeals hearing within 20 calendar days from receipt of the written appeal. Within five calendar days from the appeals hearing, the mayor shall render a written decision as to the mayor and council's decision on the appeal. 
(g)  Displayed in horse-drawn carriage. The permit issued under the provisions of this article shall be placed on display in the horse-drawn carriage to be operated by the holder of the permit, where the permit will be in clear view of the passengers at all times when the horse-drawn carriage is for hire. 
(h)  Alteration. It shall be unlawful for any person willfully to alter, deface, obliterate or destroy a horse-drawn carriage driver's permit, or cause or allow the same. 
(i)  Transfer. Any horse-drawn carriage driver's permit issued under this article is not transferable, and is to be used solely by the person to whom it is issued. 
(j)  Duration. Any horse-drawn carriage driver's permit shall be valid for that calendar year. Permits may be renewed upon application and payment of the required fee, unless the permit for the preceding period has been revoked or is under suspension. 
(k)  Suspension. The inspector shall recommend to the city clerk to suspend the driver's permit for the following reasons: 
(1)  Making any false statement in the application for the person; or 
(2)  Operating a horse-drawn carriage in violation of any provision of this article or of state law. 
The suspension by the city clerk shall be lifted upon dismissal or dropping of the charges described upon correction of the violation of any provision of this article, upon ruling in favor of the driver in any appeal hearing before the mayor and council, or at the expiration of 60 days from the date of suspension. From the decision to suspend a permit, the holder of such permit shall have the right to appeal the decision of the city clerk to the mayor and council. All suspension appeals must be filed in writing with the mayor and council within ten calendar days from the date of the suspension, and the mayor and council must convene an appeals hearing within 20 calendar days from receipt of the filing by the city clerk of the written appeal. Within five calendar days from the appeals hearing, the mayor shall render a written decision as to the mayor and council's decision on the appeal. 
(l)  Revocation. If any driver holding a permit under this article at any time ceases to meet the qualifications described in subsection (c) of this section or fails to operate his horse-drawn carriage in accordance with the provisions of this article, the city clerk shall be empowered to permanently revoke the permit. The holder of such permit shall have the right to appeal the decision of the city clerk to the mayor and council in the manner prescribed in subsection (n) of this section. 
(m)  Driving after revocation or suspension. It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a horse-drawn carriage for hire for the carriage of passengers during any period in which his permit to do so is suspended or revoked in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(n)  Appeals. Any appeal of a decision made by the city clerk to revoke a horse-drawn carriage driver's permit, pursuant to this section, shall be made in writing to the mayor and council within ten calendar days of the ruling. The mayor and council must convene an appeals hearing within 20 calendar days from the filing of the city clerk of the written appeal. The appellant shall have the right to present evidence, examine the evidence of the appellee, and to cross examine. The appellant shall have the right to be represented by counsel. Within five calendar days from the appeals hearing, the mayor shall render a written decision as to the mayor and council's decision on the appeal. 
(Code 2002, § 32-35; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-4) 
Sec. 36-24. - General identification and marking. 
Every horse-drawn carriage shall have a sign plainly painted on the rear of each vehicle. The sign shall contain the full name of the horse-drawn carriage company operating the vehicle. Additionally, the sign shall conform with all sign standards for the city and be approved by the city. 
(Code 2002, § 32-36; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-5) 
Sec. 36-25. - Safe mechanical condition required. 
Every horse-drawn carriage operated on the streets of the city shall be maintained in a safe mechanical condition, with all safety equipment remaining intact and operative at all times when the horse-drawn carriage is in service. 
(Code 2002, § 32-37; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-6) 
Sec. 36-26. - Cleanliness required. 
Each vehicle operating under this article shall be kept painted and in a clean and sanitary condition, free of litter and debris, and at all times suitable for public transportation of passengers. 
(Code 2002, § 32-38; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-7) 
Sec. 36-27. - Vehicle inspections required. 
Each horse-drawn carriage may be inspected by the inspector for compliance with the provisions of this article and shall pass the inspection before the vehicle may be used as a horse-drawn carriage in the city. Each horse-drawn carriage involved in an accident shall be inspected by the inspector before it may be returned to service transporting passengers for hire. Inspections of the horse-drawn carriages may be done at any time by the inspector. 
(Code 2002, § 32-39; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-8) 
Sec. 36-28. - Authority for removal from streets. 
The inspector shall have the authority to remove from operation on the streets of the city any vehicle used as a horse-drawn carriage which is in violation of this article, and to prohibit operation of the horse-drawn carriage until all deficiencies have been corrected. An order of the inspector to remove a vehicle from the streets may be appealed to the city clerk, and the mayor and council, as provided for in section 36-23(n). The appeal must be made in writing to the city clerk no later than ten calendar days after the inspector has exercised his authority in removing a horse-drawn carriage from the street for violation of this article. The city clerk must convene a hearing within ten calendar days of receipt of the appeal, and must render a written decision to the appellant within five calendar days of the close of the hearing. 
(Code 2002, § 32-40; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-9) 
Sec. 36-29. - Rates of fare; rate card required. 
No owner or driver of a horse-drawn carriage shall charge a greater sum for the use of the horse-drawn carriage than in accordance with the published and advertised rates, which shall be displayed in each vehicle. Rates shall be displayed in such place as to be conspicuous and to be in clear view of all passengers. 
(Code 2002, § 32-41; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-10) 
Sec. 36-30. - Driver not to leave vehicle while waiting to be hired. 
It is unlawful for any driver of any horse-drawn carriage to leave the vehicle or the immediate premises of the vehicle while the vehicle is parked and while waiting to be hired. 
(Code 2002, § 32-42; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-11) 
Sec. 36-31. - Restriction on number of passengers. 
No driver shall permit more persons to be carried in a horse-drawn carriage as passengers than the seating capacity of his horse-drawn carriage, not to exceed ten. 
(Code 2002, § 32-43; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-12) 
Sec. 36-32. - Refusal to carry orderly passengers. 
No driver shall refuse or neglect to convey any orderly person, upon request, unless previously engaged or unable or forbidden by the provisions of this article to do so. 
(Code 2002, § 32-44; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-13) 
Sec. 36-33. - Weight restrictions. 
The aggregate weight of the carriage, passengers and driver shall not exceed two times the body weight of the horse. 
(Code 2002, § 32-45; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-14) 
Sec. 36-34. - Movement of carriage prohibited under certain circumstances. 
No driver shall collect fares, make change, or take on or discharge passengers while his horse-drawn carriage is in motion. 
(Code 2002, § 32-46; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-15) 
Sec. 36-35. - Property left in carriage by passenger. 
Any horse-drawn carriage driver or operator, discovering in any horse-drawn carriage under his control, personal property which was lost or left by a passenger of such horse-drawn carriage, shall report the loss, and deliver all the property to the police department within two hours after the discovery of the property. 
(Code 2002, § 32-47; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-16) 
Sec. 36-36. - Safety equipment required. 
(a)  Each horse-drawn carriage shall be equipped with electrically powered lights or lanterns and reflectors. Such lights shall be in use when operating during the hours of darkness and when raining. The lights and reflectors shall be mounted so that they are visible from a distance of 500 feet in all directions. Each horse-drawn carriage shall have on board at all times a first aid kit. 
(b)  Each horse-drawn carriage shall be equipped with a suitable friction braking system which will enable the carriage to stop. Such braking system shall be functional and operative at all times. 
(Code 2002, § 32-48; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-17) 
Sec. 36-37. - Area of operation. 
The inspector or mayor and council may elect to set a route for horse-drawn carriages, to include a designated site for a loading and unloading stand. 
(Code 2002, § 32-49; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-18)
