Sec. 36-38. - Sanitation requirements. 
Manure and urine must be immediately treated with a chemical deodorizing solution, and manure must be removed immediately from the street by the carriage operator. Each carriage must be equipped with a suitable scoop shovel and airtight container. Horse diapers, which prevent excrement from being deposited on the street surface may be used in lieu of a scoop shovel and an airtight container at the option of the operator. In the case of horse diapers, the diapers must be approved for efficiency by the inspector before they are used. 
(Code 2002, § 32-50; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-19) 
Sec. 36-39. - Traffic violations. 
(a)  Horse-drawn carriages shall be prohibited from stopping in traffic or delaying any on-street traffic for the purposes of loading or unloading passengers or for any other purpose. 
(b)  Every person riding any animal upon a roadway and every person driving any animal-drawn vehicle within the city limits of the city shall be subject to the provisions of this article and shall operate the vehicles in accordance with the traffic laws of the city, as well as the state. 
(c)  Due to the nature of operating animal-drawn vehicles in areas of congestion and heavy traffic within the city, it shall be unlawful to operate the animal-drawn vehicles except when the animals are under complete control at all times, and shall be operated with extra caution and due care for the safety of others. 
(Code 2002, § 32-51; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-20) 
Sec. 36-40. - Impediment of traffic flow. 
It shall be unlawful for any horse-drawn carriage to willfully impede the normal flow of traffic on any city street, alley or thoroughfare at any time. Horse-drawn carriages will be required to pull immediately to the nearest curb area when one or more vehicles are unable to safely pass or continue in normal traffic flow. 
(Code 2002, § 32-52; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-21) 
Sec. 36-41. - Limits to the number of horse-drawn carriages. 
It shall be unlawful for any horse-drawn carriage company to operate more than two horse-drawn carriages for hire on the streets of the city at any given time. The city clerk may authorize more than two carriages to operate upon the company's request. Such request shall be in writing indicating the company's needs for additional carriages. The city clerk may approve the request for special events or with respect to special circumstances upon approval from the mayor and council. 
(Code 2002, § 32-53; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-22) 
Sec. 36-42. - Compliance required. 
Failure to comply with this article or any of the laws, ordinances and regulations of this city can result in the revocation of permit and punishment in municipal court. Any ordinance or laws of this city, county, state or federal agency which governs the treatment of animals, including horses or other animals of burden, must be complied with by the horse-drawn carriage operator, passengers or agents of the horse-drawn carriage company. 
(Code 2002, § 32-54; Ord. of 11-8-1999, § 67-23) 
Chapter 38 - ZONING[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— The Zoning Procedures Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-1 et seq.; local government zoning powers, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-2; conflicts of interest in zoning actions, O.C.G.A. § 36-67A-1 et seq.; effect of zoning laws on covenants running with the land, O.C.G.A. § 44-5-60; authority to adopt plans and exercise the power of zoning, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ IV. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 38-1. - Preamble and enactment clause. 
Pursuant to the authority granted by Ga. Const. art. 9, § 4, para. 2, subpara. 15, for the purpose of promoting the health, safety, convenience, order, prosperity or general welfare of the city, lessening congestion in the streets, securing safety from fire, panic and other dangers; providing adequate light and air; preventing the overcrowding of land; avoiding undue concentration of population; facilitating the adequate provision of transportation, water, sewerage, schools, parks and other public requirements; able living conditions and the sustained stability of neighborhoods; protecting property against blight and depreciation; conserving the value of buildings and structures throughout the municipality, all in accordance with the comprehensive plan, the city council does ordain and enact into law the following articles and sections. 
(Code 2002, § 34-1; Ord. of 2-10-2003, art. I) 
Sec. 38-2. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Building includes the term "structure." 
Accessory use means a use customarily incidental and subordinate to the principal use of a lot and located on the same lot as such principal use. 
Alley means a public or private service way which provides only secondary access to the rear or side of abutting property and is not intended for general traffic circulation. 
Alteration, building or structural, means any change in the supporting members of a building (such as any type of supporting structural member) except such change as may be required for its safety; any addition to a building; any change in use from that of one zoning district classification to another, or of a building from one location to another. 
Amendment by council means if the city council, by majority vote taken in a properly called council meeting, proposes to take action which will result in a zoning decision, then the city shall follow the requirements for a public hearing as set forth in this Code. 
Apartment building. See Dwelling, multifamily. 
Automobile service station means any area of land, including structures therein, used for the retail sale of gasoline or oil, automobile accessories and incidental services including facilities for lubricating, washing and cleaning, or otherwise servicing automobiles, but excluding painting and major repair. 
Basement means a story having a part but not more than one-half of its height below grade. A basement is counted as a story for the purpose of height regulations. 
Boardinghouse means a dwelling other than a hotel or motel where, for compensation and by pre-arrangement for definite periods, meals and lodging are provided for three or more persons. 
Building means any structure having a roof supported by columns or walls designed or built for the support, enclosure, shelter or protection of persons, animals, chattels or property of any kind. 
Building, accessory, means a subordinate building or a portion of the principal building, the use of which is incidental to the dominant use of the principal building on the same lot. 
Building, principal, means a building in which is conducted the main or principal use of the lot on which said building is situated. 
Building, setback line, means a line establishing the minimum allowable distance between the nearest portion of any building, excluding steps, gutters and similar fixtures, and the centerline of the abutting street on which the building faces or the right-of-way line, whichever is greater. 
Cellar means that portion of a building between floor and ceiling which is wholly or partly below grade, and having more than one-half of its height below grade. A cellar is not counted as a story for the purpose of height regulations. 
Centerline of street means that line surveyed and monumented by the proper governing authority shall be the centerline of the street or, if such a centerline has not been surveyed, it shall be that line running midway between the outside curbs or ditches of the street, or the middle of the traveled roadway of the street. 
Clinic means a building or a portion of a building where patients are not lodged overnight, but are admitted for examination and treatment by a physician or group of physicians, or a dentist or group of dentists, practicing together. 
Club, private, means a building, or portion thereof, or premises owned or operated by a corporation, association, or person for a social, educational or recreational purpose, but primarily for profit or to render a service which is customarily carried on as a business. 
Day care center means any place operated by a person, society, agency, corporation or institution, or any other group wherein are received for pay five or more children under 18 years of age for group care, without transfer of custody, for more than four hours, but less than 24 hours, for more than one consecutive day. 
District means any section of the city within which the zoning regulations are uniform. 
Dwelling means a building or portion thereof designed, arranged or used principally for residential occupancy, but not including mobile homes. 
Dwelling, high density residential, means a building designed for and occupied by 11 or more families. 
Dwelling, multifamily, means a building designed for and occupied exclusively by three to ten families. 
Dwelling, single-family, means a building designed for and occupied exclusively by one family. 
Dwelling, two-family (duplex), means a building designed for and occupied exclusively by two families. 
Dwelling unit means one or more rooms located within a building and forming a single habitable unit with facilities which are used or intended to be used for living, sleeping, cooking and eating purposes. 
Family means one or more persons occupying a dwelling and living as a single housekeeping unit, all of whom or all but two of whom are related to each other by birth, adoption or marriage as distinguished from a group occupying a boardinghouse, roominghouse, hotel or motel, as herein defined. 
Flea market means an activity where stalls or spaces within the bounds of a specific location are made available to the vendor of handicraft items or the vendors of new merchandise where each new item does not have a price in excess of $50.00, or to vendors of secondhand items. All such vendors may not be manufacturers or the holders of any other retail license for the sale of similar merchandise. 
Flea market stand means that part of an individual lot which has been reserved for the placement of flea market booths, appurtenant structures or additions. 
Floodplain means an area within the intermediate regional flood contour elevations subject to periodic flooding as designated by the U.S. Geological Survey of Flood Prone Areas for the Department of Housing and Urban Development and other government agencies. 
Floor area, commercial, business, and industrial, means the sum of the gross horizontal areas of the several floors of a building measured from the exterior faces of the exterior walls, or from the centerline of walls separating two buildings. 
Floor area, residential, means the gross horizontal areas of the several floors of a dwelling, measured from the exterior faces of the exterior walls, including habitable basements, but excluding garages, carports and porches. 
Garage apartment means a dwelling unit for one family erected above a private garage detached from the main dwelling. 
Garage, auto repair, means a building or portion thereof, other than a private or parking garage, designed or used for the storage, servicing, repairing, equipping and hiring of motor driven vehicles. 
Garage, private, means an accessory building designed or used for the storage of motor-driven vehicles owned and used by the occupants of the building to which it is accessory. 
Home occupation means an occupation for gain or support conducted only by members of a family residing on the premises and entirely within the main dwelling. 
Hotel means a building in which lodging is provided and offered to the public for compensation and in which ingress and egress to and from all rooms are made through an inside lobby or office supervised by a person in charge at all hours. A hotel is open to the transient public, as opposed to a boardinghouse or a roominghouse, which are herein separately defined. 
Institution means premises occupied by a not-for-profit corporation or establishment for public or semi-public use. 
Junkyard means a lot, land or structure, or part thereof, used primarily for the collecting, storage and sale of waste paper, rags, scrap metal or discarded material; or for the collecting, dismantling, storage and salvaging of machinery or vehicles not in running condition, or for the sale of parts thereof. 
Loading space means a space having a minimum dimension of 12 feet by 35 feet and a vertical clearance of at least 14 feet within the main building or on the same lot, providing for the standing, loading or unloading of trucks. 
Lot means a portion of land occupied or intended to be occupied by a common use, or occupied or intended to be occupied by a building or group of buildings devoted to a common use, together with the customary accessory buildings and uses, parking spaces, and open spaces belonging to the same and having its principal frontage upon a street. The term "lot" includes the terms "plot" and "parcel." 
Lot, corner, means a lot abutting two or more streets at their intersection. 
Lot, through, means a lot, other than a corner lot, abutting two streets. 
Lot of record means a lot, the boundaries of which were filed as a legal record, whether by subdivision plat or by metes and bounds, at the time of adoption of the ordinances from which this chapter is derived. 
Lot width means the width of the lot at the front building setback line. 
Major street means a street or highway being a part of the system of principal streets as shown on the zoning map. 
Manufactured home means any vehicle or similar structure originally designed or intended to be portable and constructed so as to permit continued occupancy for dwelling or sleeping purposes, sometimes called "house trailers," but not including a trailer temporarily for recreation purposes. Also termed "mobile home." 
Manufactured home park means any area planned and developed for the exclusive use of non-transient mobile homes, approved by the mayor and council, which conforms to the regulations set forth in this chapter. Also termed "mobile home park." 
Modular home means a factory-fabricated transportable building consisting of units designed to be incorporated at a building site on a permanent foundation into a permanent structure to be used for residential purposes. 
Motel means a building or group of buildings used for temporary occupancy of transients and containing no facilities for cooking in the individual units. 
Nonconforming use means any building or land lawfully occupied by a use at the time of passage of this chapter, or amendment thereto, but which does not conform, after the passage of this chapter or amendment thereto, to the use regulations of the district in which it is situated. 
Nursery school or kindergarten means any premises or portion thereof used for educational work or part-time care of children of less than the age required for enrollment in the public school system. 
Nursing home means a home for the aged or infirm in which three or more persons not of the immediate family are received, kept or provided with food and shelter or care for compensation, but not including hospitals, clinics or similar establishments devoted primarily to the diagnosis and treatment of the sick or injured. 
Open space means a yard area which is not used for or occupied by a driveway, off-street parking, loading space, drying yard or refuse storage space. 
Outdoor advertising sign means any sign used as an outdoor display for the purpose of making anything known, the mater advertised or displayed being remote from its origin or point of sale. 
Parking area means an open, unoccupied space used or required for use for parking of vehicles exclusively and in which no gasoline or vehicular accessories are sold or no other business is conducted and no fees are charged. 
Parking lot means an open area used exclusively for the temporary storage of motor vehicles and within which motor fuels and oils may be sold and fees charged; but no vehicles are to be equipped, repaired, rented or sold. 
Parking space means a space, enclosed or unenclosed, having an area of not less than 200 square feet exclusive of driveways and maneuvering areas, permanently reserved for the temporary storage of one vehicle and connected with a street or alley by a driveway. 
Principal use means the primary purpose for which land on a building is used. 
Premises means a lot, together with all buildings and structures existing thereon. 
Roominghouse means a building other than a hotel or motel where lodging for three or more persons not of the immediate family is provided for pre-arranged definite periods and for compensation. 
Sign means a name, identification, description, display or illustration which is affixed to, painted or represented, directly or indirectly, upon a building, structure, parcel or lot and which directs attention to an object, product, place, activity, person, institution, organization or business located on the premises. The term "sign" shall not be deemed to include official court or governmental notices or the flag emblem or insignia of a nation political unit, school or religion. 
Specialty shop means a retail sales establishment with primary sales of craft, apparel, gift, accessory, furniture, furnishings and other like items, to the public with emphasis on tourist and visitor shoppers. 
Street means a public way for vehicular traffic that is open to the general public and which affords the principal means of access to abutting property. 
Street line means the dividing line between a lot, tract or parcel of land and a contiguous street. 
Structure means anything constructed or erected, the use of which requires a location on the ground, or attached to something having a location on the ground. 
Trailer court. See Mobile home park. 
Trailer house. See Mobile home. 
Travel trailer means a vehicular portable structure designed as a temporary dwelling for travel, recreational and vacation uses; is not more than eight feet in body width and is of any weight, provided its body length does not exceed 29 feet. 
Travel trailer park means any lot on which are temporarily parked two or more travel trailers for a period of less than 30 days. 
Used or occupied, as applied to any land or building, includes the term "intended," "arranged," or "designed to be used or occupied." 
Yard means a space on the same lot with a principal building, open, unoccupied and unobstructed by buildings or structures from ground to sky except where encroachments and accessory buildings are expressly permitted. 
Yard, front, means a yard extending the full width of the lot and situated between the right-of-way line of the abutting street and the front line of the principal building. 
Yard, rear, means a yard extending the full width of the lot at the rear line of the principal building from the rear line of the lot to the nearest point of the principal building. 
Yard, side, means a yard situated between the principal building and side line of the lot extending from the rear line of the front yard to the front line of the rear yard. 
Zoning decision means final action by the city council which results in: 
(1)  The adoption of a zoning ordinance; 
(2)  The adoption of an amendment to a zoning ordinance which changes the text of the zoning ordinance; or 
(3)  The adoption of an amendment to a zoning ordinance which rezones property from one zoning classification to another. 
(Code 2002, § 34-3; Ord. of 2-10-2003, art. III) 
Secs. 38-3—38-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - APPLICATION OF REGULATIONS 

Sec. 38-23. - Use. 
Except as hereinafter provided, no building or parcel of land shall hereafter be used or occupied and no building or part thereof shall be erected, moved or altered except for a use permitted within the zoning district in which it is located. 
(Code 2002, § 34-21; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 4.1) 
Sec. 38-24. - Height and density. 
Except as hereinafter provided, no building shall hereafter be erected or altered so as to exceed the height limit for the zoning district in which it is located, nor shall any building or lot be used or occupied hereafter for more families than permitted in the zoning district in which it is located. 
(Code 2002, § 34-22; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 4.2) 
Sec. 38-25. - Yard occupancy. 
Except as hereinafter provided, no building shall hereafter be erected or altered so as to occupy any required yard, nor shall any side, rear or front yard be narrower or smaller than is required for the zoning district in which it is located, except as provided in section 38-254. 
(Code 2002, § 34-23; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 4.3) 
Sec. 38-26. - Yard use limitation. 
Except as hereinafter provided, no yard or other open space provided about any building for the purpose of complying with the regulations of this article shall be included as a part of a yard or other open space for any other building. 
(Code 2002, § 34-24; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 4.4) 
Sec. 38-27. - Jurisdiction. 
The provisions of this article shall govern the location and use of buildings, structures and land within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Code 2002, § 34-25; Ord. of 2-10-2003, 4.5) 
Sec. 38-28. - Public street frontage. 
No building shall be erected on a lot which does not abut for at least 25 feet on a public street. 
(Code 2002, § 34-26; Ord. of 2-10-2003, 4.6) 
Sec. 38-29. - Necessary repairs permitted. 
Nothing in this article shall prevent the strengthening of restoration to a safe or lawful condition of any part of any building or structure declared unsafe or unlawful by the building official, the fire chief, or any other duly authorized city official. 
(Code 2002, § 34-27; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 4.7) 
Sec. 38-30. - Prohibited when not specified. 
If not otherwise stated, it is the intent of this article that any use not specifically permitted in a use district as provided under article IV of this chapter shall be prohibited in that district. The board of zoning appeals shall decide specific judgements about the placement of a disputed use. 
(Code 2002, § 34-28; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 4.8) 
Secs. 38-31—38-48. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - GENERAL PROVISIONS 

Sec. 38-49. - One principal building per lot. 
Within residential zoning districts, excepting group developments as provided for in section 38-257, no more than one principal building with its customary accessory buildings may occupy, or be constructed upon, any lot. 
(Code 2002, § 34-41; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.1) 
Sec. 38-50. - Reduction in lot area. 
No lot may be reduced in area below the minimum lot area as specified herein for the zoning district within which said lot is located. 
(Code 2002, § 34-42; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.2) 
Sec. 38-51. - Yard requirements of accessory buildings. 
The minimum yard requirements of this article also apply to accessory buildings. However, accessory buildings may be located within rear yards to within five feet of a rear or side lot line. 
(Code 2002, § 34-43; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.3) 
Sec. 38-52. - Attachment of accessory buildings to principal buildings. 
When an accessory building is attached to the principal building by a breezeway, passageway or similar means, it shall comply with the yard requirements of the principal building to which it is attached. 
(Code 2002, § 34-44; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.4) 
Sec. 38-53. - Distance between buildings. 
Except as herein provided, no accessory building shall be located closer than ten feet to a principal building or to any other accessory building. 
(Code 2002, § 34-45; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.5) 
Sec. 38-54. - Frontage on corner lots and double frontage lots. 
On lots having frontage on more than one street, the minimum front yard shall be provided for each street in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 2002, § 34-46; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.6) 
Sec. 38-55. - Street access. 
No building shall hereafter be constructed on a lot that does not have frontage on a publicly dedicated and maintained street. 
(Code 2002, § 34-47; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.7) 
Sec. 38-56. - Corner visibility clearance. 
No fence, structure, sign, planting or other construction above a height of 3½ feet shall be maintained within 20 feet of the intersection of the right-of-way lines of two streets or railroads, or of a street intersection with a railroad right-of-way. 
(Code 2002, § 34-48; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.8) 
Sec. 38-57. - Fences and walls. 
No fence or freestanding wall, other than a retaining wall, shall be more than eight feet in height in a residential district. 
(Code 2002, § 34-49; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.9) 
Sec. 38-58. - Construction of temporary buildings. 
Temporary buildings used in conjunction with construction work may be permitted in any district but shall be removed immediately upon completion of the construction. 
(Code 2002, § 34-50; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.10) 
Sec. 38-59. - Projections into yards. 
(a)  Every part of a required yard shall be open to the sky and unobstructed, except for the ordinary projections of sills, belt courses, cornices, eaves, chimneys, stoops, buttresses and other ornamental and architectural features, provided that such features do not project more than three feet into any required yard. 
(b)  Accessory buildings may project into yards, provided that no accessory building may be closer than five feet to a lot line. 
(c)  An open, unroofed porch or paved terrace may project into a required front or rear yard for a distance not to exceed ten feet, and into a side yard to a point not closer than five feet from any side lot line. 
(Code 2002, § 34-51; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 5.11) 
Secs. 38-60—38-76. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ESTABLISHMENT OF ZONING DISTRICTS 

Sec. 38-77. - Zoning districts. 
For the purpose of this article, the city is divided into the following zoning districts: 

 
(Code 2002, § 34-71; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 6.1; Ord. of 4-11-2005(2)) 
Sec. 38-78. - Zoning district boundaries. 
The boundaries of each zoning district are hereby established as shown on a map entitled "Zoning Districts Map of the City of Warm Springs, Georgia," adopted by the city council and certified by the city clerk. Said map and all explanatory matter thereon accompanies and is hereby made a part of this chapter and shall be on file in the city hall. 
(Code 2002, § 34-72; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 6.2) 
Sec. 38-79. - Rules for determining boundaries of zoning districts. 
Where uncertainty exists with respect to the exact location of the boundary of any zoning district shown on the zoning map, the following rules shall apply: 
(1)  Where a boundary is indicated as approximately following the centerline of a street, or a railroad, or a drainage course, such centerline shall be construed to be the boundary. 
(2)  Where a boundary is indicated as approximately following a lot line, such lot line shall be construed to be the boundary. 
(3)  Where the location of a boundary is not otherwise indicated as specified above, or dimensioned on the zoning map, said boundary shall be located by use of the scale on the zoning map. 
(4)  Where a public street, road or alley is officially vacated or abandoned, the zoning regulations applicable to the property to which it is reverted shall apply to such vacated or abandoned street, road or alley. 
(Code 2002, § 34-73; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 6.3) 
Secs. 38-80—38-101. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - USES PERMITTED IN ZONING DISTRICTS 

Sec. 38-102. - Uses permitted. 
The uses permitted in each of the zoning districts shall be only those listed in this article. 
(Code 2002, § 34-91; Ord. of 2-10-2003, art. VII) 
Sec. 38-103. - R-1 Residential, Single-Family. 
(a)  The following uses are permitted in the R-1 district: 
(1)  Single-family dwellings, excluding mobile homes, with a minimum of 1,200 square feet of living space. 
(2)  Accessory buildings and uses when located on the same lot or parcel of land as the principal building and provided the requirements of article VII of this chapter are met. 
(3)  Home occupation. 
(4)  Public utility installations and lands. 
(5)  Nurseries and truck gardens, except that no retail sales shall be made on the premises. 
(6)  Forest and agricultural uses except commercial dairies. Livestock is permitted in accordance with chapter 6. All livestock shall be fenced in an acceptable manner. 
(7)  Day care centers, provided that the requirements set forth in article VII of this chapter are met. 
(8)  Passive recreation areas. 
(9)  Home swimming pools, provided the location is not closer than ten feet to any property line and the pool is enclosed by a wall or fence at least four feet in height. 
(b)  Minimum lot requirements specified in article VI of this chapter must be met. 
(Code 2002, § 34-92; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 7.1) 
Sec. 38-104. - R-2 Residential, Two-Family. 
(a)  All uses permitted in R-1, subject to restrictions set forth in section 38-103; and: 
(1)  Two-family dwellings, provided that each dwelling unit has a minimum of 1,000 square feet of total living space. 
(2)  Public parks, playgrounds, community buildings and similar public service facilities serving residential areas. 
(3)  Cemeteries, provided that the requirements set forth in article VII of this chapter are met. 
(4)  Schools, public and private. 
(5)  Private, not-for-profit clubs or lodges when located on at least two acres, and when any building or activity related thereto is located at least 50 feet from the nearest lot line. 
(6)  Hospitals, nursing and convalescent homes and charitable or philanthropic institutions, when located on at least one acre, and when any building or activity related thereto is located at least 50 feet from the nearest lot line. 
(7)  Riding stables and academies, when located on at least 20 acres, and when any building or activity related thereto is located at least 50 feet from the nearest lot line. 
(8)  Public or private golf courses, except miniature courses or driving ranges operated for commercial purposes. 
(9)  Churches, when located on at least one acre, and when any building or activity related thereto is located at least 50 feet from the nearest lot line. 
(b)  Minimum lot requirements specified in article VI of this chapter must be met. 
(Code 2002, § 34-93; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 7.2) 
Sec. 38-105. - R-3 Residential, Multifamily. 
(a)  All uses permitted in R-1 and R-2, subject to the restrictions set forth in sections 38-103 and 38-104; and: 
(1)  Multifamily dwellings, provided that each dwelling unit has a minimum of 750 square feet of total living space. 
(2)  Roominghouses or boardinghouses. 
(3)  Mobile homes and mobile home parks, provided the requirements set forth in article VII of this chapter are met. 
(4)  Office buildings exclusively used for professional occupancy, and of such character and nature that such use will not adversely affect adjacent and nearby residential properties. 
(5)  Automobile service stations. 
(6)  Hotels and motels. 
(7)  Travel trailer parks, provided they meet the requirements set forth in article VII of this chapter. 
(b)  Minimum lot requirements specified in article VI of this chapter must be met. 
(Code 2002, § 34-94; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 7.3) 
Sec. 38-106. - R-4 Planned Unit Development. 
The following uses are permitted in the R-4 district: 
(1)  Single-family dwellings. 
(2)  Townhomes. 
(3)  Golf, country club, pool and recreation court. 
(4)  Community facilities. 
(5)  Accessory retail and service uses, located wholly within a building, and limited to convenience retail and service establishments such as pro shops, personal services, and restaurants accessory to a club, or as permitted by council. No outdoor advertising is allowed. 
(Code 2002, § 34-95; Ord. of 4-11-2005(2)) 
Sec. 38-107. - C-1 Commercial. 
All uses permitted in R-1, R-2 and R-3, subject to the restrictions set forth in sections 38-103 through 38-105; and: 
(1)  Specialty shops. 
(2)  Restaurants. 
(3)  Banking and lending institutions. 
(4)  Florists. 
(5)  Miniature golf courses. 
(6)  Driving ranges. 
(7)  Photography studios. 
(8)  Commercial parking lots. 
(9)  Service businesses. 
(Code 2002, § 34-96; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 7.4; Ord. of 4-11-2005(2); Ord. of 8-9-2005) 
Sec. 38-108. - C-2 Commercial. 
All uses permitted in R-1, R-2, R-3, and C-1, subject to the restrictions set forth in sections 38-103, 38-104, 38-105 and 38-107, and: 
(1)  Retail stores. 
(2)  Amusement and recreation businesses, including theaters, but not including drive-in theaters. 
(3)  Hardware or building material sales. 
(4)  Personal services. 
(5)  Business, music, art and dancing schools. 
(6)  Clinics, veterinarian offices, but not outside kennels. 
(7)  Laundry and dry cleaning services, including coin-operated laundromats. 
(8)  Repair services. 
(9)  Commercial parking lots, private vehicle storage and parking spaces. 
(10)  Mortuaries. 
(11)  Lodges and organizational meeting halls. 
(12)  Millenary, dressmaking and tailoring activities. 
(13)  Food stores, including supermarkets with off-street parking and loading for vehicles in operating condition. 
(14)  Retail sales of new or used cars and trucks in operating condition. 
(15)  Bus terminals, railroad terminals and freight terminals, except truck terminals. 
(16)  Wholesale businesses, including display and storage. 
(17)  Tire retreading and recapping establishments, provided that no building for such use shall have any opening, other than stationary windows, within 100 feet of a residential district. 
(Code 2002, § 34-97; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 7.5; Ord. of 4-11-2005(2)) 
Sec. 38-109. - I Industrial. 
The following uses are permitted in the I district: 
(1)  Agriculture. 
(2)  Carpentry, plumbing and painting shops. 
(3)  Construction and contractor's yards. 
(4)  Storage or warehousing facilities. 
(5)  Service businesses. 
(6)  Wholesale businesses. 
(7)  Building materials storage or wholesaling. 
(8)  Lumber yards. 
(9)  Broadcasting towers. 
(10)  Truck terminals. 
(11)  Bottling plants and dairy products processing plants. 
(12)  Petroleum products storage and sales. 
(13)  Automotive, farm implement, mobile home and trailer sales, service and repair. 
(14)  Grain and feed storage. 
(15)  Heating fuel or building material storage and/or wholesaling, provided that the materials shall not be extracted or processed on the premises. 
(16)  Public utility installations and lands. 
(17)  Assembly of parts for production of finished equipment. 
(18)  Manufacturing, fabricating, processing, assembling, repair or servicing of any product or commodity. 
(19)  Research institutions and laboratories. 
(20)  Animal hospitals and veterinarian clinics with kennels. 
(21)  Cold storage plants. 
(22)  Laundry and dry cleaning plants. 
(23)  Drive-in theaters. 
(24)  Banks and lending institutions. 
(25)  Restaurants and drive-in restaurants. 
(26)  Greenhouses and florist shops. 
(27)  Off-street parking and loading for vehicles in operating condition. 
(28)  Junkyards, including automobile wrecking or salvage yards, when completely enclosed by a solid fence having a minimum height of six feet, but in no case less than such height as will screen all operations from view, and located no closer than 200 feet to a residential zoning district. Said solid fence shall be at least 25 feet from any street or highway right-of-way. 
(29)  Sexually oriented businesses. 
(Code 2002, § 34-98; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 7.6; Ord. of 4-11-2005(2); Ord. No. 09-05, 10-14-2009) 
Secs. 38-110—38-131. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - DIMENSIONAL REQUIREMENTS IN ZONING DISTRICTS 

Sec. 38-132. - Dimensional requirements. 
Dimensional requirements for zoning districts and mobile home parks are set out below: 

 
(Code 2002, § 34-121; Ord. of 2-10-2003, art. VI; Ord. of 4-11-2005(2); Ord. of 3-14-2006) 
Secs. 38-133—38-162. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - SPECIAL PROVISIONS 

Sec. 38-163. - Accessory buildings. 
The location of accessory buildings and uses in residential districts shall meet the following requirements: 
(1)  Where an accessory building is attached to the main building, a substantial part of one wall of the accessory building shall be an integral part of the main building, or such accessory building shall be attached to the main building in a substantial manner by a roof and, therefore, subject to the requirements applicable to the main building. 
(2)  A detached accessory building shall not be closer than ten feet to the main building, nor closer than five feet to the lot line. 
(3)  A detached accessory building not more than two stories in height may be constructed on not more than 30 percent of the rear yard. 
(4)  No detached accessory building may be located on the front yard of a lot, nor the side yards except for detached garages. 
(Code 2002, § 34-141; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 9.1) 
Sec. 38-164. - Temporary buildings. 
Temporary buildings used in conjunction with construction work only may be permitted in any district and shall be removed immediately upon completion of construction. 
(Code 2002, § 34-142; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 9.2) 
Sec. 38-165. - Day care centers. 
Any dwelling acting as a part-time or full-time day care center must be approved by the local board of health and those serving five or more children under 18 years of age for pay must meet the requirements set forth by the state department of human resources. All centers must have a fenced area of at least four feet in height that encloses the area where the children are to be allowed outside. 
(Code 2002, § 34-143; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 9.3) 
Sec. 38-166. - Cemeteries. 
(a)  The site proposed for a cemetery shall not interfere with the development of a system of collector or larger streets in the vicinity of such site. 
(b)  Any new cemetery shall be located on a site containing not less than five acres. 
(c)  All structures shall be set back no less than 25 feet from any property line or street right-of-way line. 
(d)  All graves or burial lots shall be set back no less than 25 feet from any property line or minor street right-of-way lines, and not less than 50 feet from any collector, arterial, expressway or freeway right-of-way line. 
(e)  The entire cemetery property shall be landscaped and maintained. 
(Code 2002, § 34-144; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 9.4) 
Sec. 38-167. - Manufactured (mobile) homes. 
(a)  The lot area and dimensions must meet the requirements of a single-family dwelling unit within the district in which the mobile home unit is located. 
(b)  In no case shall the unit be located within 30 feet of any permanent principal building. 
(c)  The mobile home unit must be supported under all exterior walls by a permanent foundation, completely enclosing the undercarriage, and must be connected to all available public facilities or have an approved water and sewerage system by the county board of health. 
(d)  Mobile homes placed subsequent to the adoption of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived shall have a front porch not less than five feet by seven feet, a rear porch not less than four feet by six feet, and shall have steps and handrails around the porches and steps. 
(e)  A single mobile home may be used for an office in the subdivision by the developer, temporary residence during construction of permanent residency, or for other special purposes, for a period not to exceed six months upon written approval from the building inspector. 
(Code 2002, § 34-145; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 9.5; Ord. of 10-12-2010, § 1) 
Sec. 38-168. - Pre-owned manufactured (mobile) homes. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Applicant means any person seeking to install a pre-owned manufactured home in the city limits. 
Building inspector means the person appointed, employed, or otherwise designated as the director of planning, permits and inspections; the municipal building official or any of his assistants. 
Certificate of occupancy means a document issued by the building inspector certifying that a pre-owned manufactured home is in compliance with applicable requirements set forth by this article, and indicating it to be in a condition suitable for residential occupancy. 
Guarantee of condition bond means a surety bond to guarantee that the affidavit and photographs required by subsections (c)(1)a and b of this section reasonably portray or represents the existing condition of the pre-owned manufactured home proposed for relocation. In lieu of the bond, a cash deposit may be deposited with the city. 
Install means to construct a foundation system and to place or erect a manufactured home on such foundation system. The term "install" includes, without limitation, supporting, blocking, leveling, securing, or anchoring such manufactured home and connecting multiple or expandable sections of such manufactured home. 
Jurisdiction means the areas within the city limits of the city. 
Manufactured home means a structure, transportable in one or more sections, which, in the traveling mode, is eight body feet or more in width or 40 body feet or more in length or, when erected on site, is 320 or more square feet and which is built on a permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling with or without a permanent foundation when connected to the required utilities and includes the plumbing, heating, air-conditioning, and electrical systems contained therein; except that the term "manufactured home" shall include any structure which meets all the requirements of this subsection except the size requirements and with respect to which the manufacturer voluntarily files a certification required by the Secretary of Housing and Urban Development and complies with the standards established under the National Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act of 1974, 42 USC 5401 et seq. 
Pre-owned manufactured home means any manufactured home that has been previously used as a residential dwelling and has been titled. 
(b)  Conditions. All pre-owned manufactured homes located in the jurisdiction shall bear a label certifying it was constructed in compliance with the National Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act of 1974, 42 USC 5401 et seq. (the HUD Code) and shall be installed in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 8-2-160 et seq. 
(c)  Permitting, inspection, certificate of occupancy and fees. A permit shall be required to locate a pre-owned manufactured home in the jurisdiction. 
(1)  Permit. To obtain a permit, applicants shall provide to the building inspector: 
a.  An affidavit signed by the applicant that the pre-owned manufactured home meets health and safety standards required by this Act; 
b.  Photographs of the interior and exterior of the pre-owned manufactured home providing evidence that home meets the minimum health and safety standards of subsection (d) of section; 
c.  A $1,000.00 refundable guarantee of condition bond or $1,000.00 refundable cash deposit; and 
d.  The permit and inspection fee required by subsection (c)(4) of this section. 
(2)  Inspection. Upon receipt of a permit, applicants may relocate the manufactured home on a residential site for the purposes of inspection. The applicant shall arrange for an inspection to be held once the installation of the manufactured home is complete. 
(3)  Certificate of occupancy. A certificate of occupancy shall be issued to the applicant at such time that the building inspector certifies that the requirements of this article have been met. 
(4)  Fee. A permit and inspection fee of $35.00 shall be charged to the applicant to cover the cost to the city to process the permit application and inspect the pre-owned manufactured home. Such fee shall cover the initial inspection and one follow-up inspection. The applicant shall be charged the estimated value of work plus two inspections for each additional follow-up inspection that may be necessary. 
(5)  Alternative inspection. At the request of the applicant, the building inspector may, at his discretion, inspect a pre-owned manufactured home prior to its being relocated if the home is then located at another site within the city. 
(d)  Minimum health and safety standards. All preowned manufactured homes shall comply with the following before being issued a certificate of occupancy by the building inspector: 
(1)  HUD Code. Every pre-owned manufactured home located in the jurisdiction shall be in compliance with the Federal Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act, 42 USC 5401—5445 (the HUD Code) and shall not have been altered in such a way that the home no longer meets the HUD Code. 
(2)  Interior condition. Every floor, interior wall, and ceiling of a pre-owned manufactured home shall be in sound condition. Doors and windows shall be operable, watertight and in good working condition. The floor system shall be in sound condition and free of warping, holes, water damage, or deterioration. 
(3)  Exterior condition. The exterior of all pre-owned manufactured homes shall be free of loose or rotting boards or timbers and any other conditions that might admit rain or moisture to the interior portions of the walls or to occupied spaces. The exterior siding shall be free of rot and rust. Roofs shall be structurally sound and have no obvious defects that might admit rain or cause moisture to collect on the interior portion of the home. 
(4)  Sanitary facilities. Every plumbing fixture, water, and waste pipe of a pre-owned manufactured home shall be in a sanitary working condition when properly connected, and shall be free from leaks and obstructions. Each home shall contain a kitchen sink. Each bathroom shall contain a lavatory and water closet. At least one bathroom shall contain a tub and/or shower facilities. Each of these fixtures shall be checked upon being connected to ensure they are in good working condition. 
(5)  Heating systems. Heating shall be safe and in working condition. Unvented heaters shall be prohibited. 
(6)  Electrical systems. Switches, receptacles, fixtures, etc., shall be properly installed and wired and shall be in working condition. Distribution panels shall be in compliance with the approved listing, complete with required breakers, with all unused openings covered with solid covers approved and listed for that purpose. The home shall be subject to an electrical continuity test to ensure that all metallic parts are properly bonded. 
(7)  Hot water supply. Each home shall contain a water heater in safe and working condition. 
(8)  Egress windows. Each bedroom of a manufactured home shall have at least one operable window of sufficient size to allow egress if necessary. 
(9)  Ventilation. The kitchen in the home shall have at least one operating window or other ventilation device. 
(10)  Smoke detectors. Each pre-owned manufactured home shall contain one operable battery-powered smoke detector in each bedroom and in the kitchen, which must be installed in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendations. 
(e)  Enforcement. 
(1)  Permanent connection to utilities shall not be approved until the building inspector has issued a certificate of occupancy. 
(2)  Owners of pre-owned manufactured homes that are not in compliance upon a third inspection shall have their permit revoked and shall be required to remove the home from the jurisdiction at their own expense. 
(3)  The guarantee of condition bond or cash deposit will be forfeited after 90 days from the date of inspection, unless all conditions and standards are met prior to the end of the 90 days or an extension has been issued in writing by the building inspector. 
(f)  Penalties. Failure to remove a pre-owned manufactured home from the jurisdiction upon failure to receive a certificate of occupancy shall be punishable by a fine according to the general penalties provision of this Code. Each day any violation under this article continues shall be considered a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 10-12-2010, § 2(145.1)) 
Sec. 38-169. - Mobile home parks. 
(a)  The minimum lot area per park shall be 320,000 square feet, and the minimum lot width for that portion used for entrance and exit shall be 50 feet. The minimum lot width for that portion containing mobile home spaces or stands shall be 40 feet. 
(b)  The minimum number of spaces completed and ready for occupancy before the first occupancy is permitted shall be 30 spaces. The minimum area for each mobile home space or stand shall be 3,500 square feet. 
(c)  No space shall be rented for residential use of a mobile home in any such park except for periods of 30 days or more. No mobile home shall be admitted to any park unless it can be demonstrated that it meets the requirements of any additional laws and ordinances adopted by the city council. 
(d)  Convenience establishments of a commercial nature, including stores, laundry and dry cleaning establishments and pick-up laundry and dry cleaning agencies, and beauty shops and barbershops may be permitted in mobile home parks, provided that such establishments and the parking areas primarily related to their operations: 
(1)  Shall not occupy more than ten percent of the area of the park; 
(2)  Shall be subordinate to the residential use and character of the park; 
(3)  Shall be located, designed and intended to serve frequent trade or service needs or persons residing in the park; and 
(4)  Shall present no visible evidence of their commercial character from any portion of any residential district outside the park. 
(Code 2002, § 34-146; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 9.6) 
Sec. 38-170. - Travel trailer parks. 
In any district where travel trailer parks are permitted, the applicant shall submit a layout of the park, subject to the following conditions: 
(1)  No travel trailer park shall be located without direct access to a county, state or federal highway, with a minimum lot width of not less than 50 feet for that portion used for entrance and exit. No entrance or exit shall be through a residential district, nor require movement of traffic from the park through a residential district. 
(2)  The minimum lot area per park shall be three acres. 
(3)  Spaces in travel trailer parks may be used by travel trailers, provided they meet any additional laws and ordinances of the city council, and shall be rented by the day or week only. An occupant of such space shall remain in the same trailer park for a period of not more than 30 days. 
(4)  Management headquarters, recreational facilities, toilets, showers, laundry facilities and other uses and structures customarily incidental to operation of a trailer park are permitted as accessory uses, provided: 
a.  Such establishments and the parking area primarily related to their operations shall not occupy more than ten percent of the area of the park; 
b.  Such establishments shall be restricted in their use to occupants of the park; and 
c.  Such establishments shall present no visible evidence of their commercial character that would attract customers other than occupants of the park. 
(5)  No space shall be so located that any part intended for occupancy for sleeping purposes shall be within 50 feet of the right-of-way line of any freeway, expressway or collector street, or of any minor street. 
(6)  A certificate of approval of the county board of health shall accompany the travel trailer park site plan. 
(Code 2002, § 34-147; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 9.7) 
Sec. 38-171. - Planned unit development. 
(a)  Development plan. The development plan shall be the zoning control document for features depicted graphically. The site plan requirement applicable to rezoning requests shall be adhered to for PUD rezoning requests. A site plan shall become the development plan if the request to rezone is approved without changes or additions. If the approval by the city council differs in any way from what is depicted on the site plan submitted for the purpose of seeking rezoning, a revised plan must be certified by the city council before related development permits may be issued. A site plan or development plan shall not substitute for plans which are required as a prerequisite for applying for development related permits. The location of all use areas shall be shown on the development plan, and location on the ground shall be as shown on the development plan. 
(b)  Development standards. 
(1)  Minimum PUD size: 20 contiguous acres. 
(2)  Maximum density: 
a.  Single-family: Five units per gross acre. 
b.  Townhomes: Eight units per gross acre. 
(3)  All other standards shall be as specified in the development chapter (chapter 20) and elsewhere in this article. 
(Code 2002, § 34-148; Ord. of 4-11-2005(2)) 
Secs. 38-172—38-195. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - OFF-STREET PARKING AND LOADING 

Sec. 38-196. - General requirements. 
(a)  Off-street parking facilities for one- and two-family dwellings shall be located on the same lot or plot of ground as the building to be served. The location of off-street parking facilities for other than one- and two-family dwellings shall not be more than 300 feet distant measured along the nearest pedestrian walkway. 
(b)  Parking requirements for two or more uses of the same or different types may be satisfied by the allocation of a common or collective parking facility. Such facility shall not be less than the sum of the requirements for the individual uses computed separately in accordance with the requirements of this article. 
(c)  For the purposes of this article, the term "off-street parking space" shall consist of an area of not less than 200 square feet exclusive of driveways and maneuvering areas permanently reserved for the temporary storage of one vehicle and connected with a street or alley by a driveway. 
(d)  For the purposes of this article, the term "off-street loading space" shall consist of a space having direct access to an alley or street and having the following minimum dimensions: 
(1)  Length: 35 feet; 
(2)  Width: 12 feet; 
(3)  Vertical clearance : 14 feet. 
(e)  Areas reserved for off-street parking or loading in accordance with the provisions of this section shall not be reduced in area or changed to any other use unless the permitted use which it serves is discontinued or modified, except where equivalent off-street parking or loading space is provided. 
(f)  For uses not specifically mentioned in this section, the requirements for off-street parking and loading facilities for a similar use specifically mentioned in this section shall apply. 
(Code 2002, § 34-161; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 10.1) 
Sec. 38-197. - Off-street parking requirements. 
At the time of the erection of any building or structure, there shall be provided off-street parking spaces with adequate provision for ingress and egress by an automobile of standard size, in accordance with the schedule below. When a building or structure is enlarged or increased in capacity by adding dwelling rooms, guestrooms, floor area or seats, minimum off-street parking shall be provided for such additional rooms, floor area or seats. 

 
(Code 2002, § 34-162; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 10.2) 
Sec. 38-198. - Off-street loading spaces. 
Every building used for business, trade or industry shall provide spaces as indicated below for the loading and unloading of vehicles off the street or public alley. Such space shall have access to a public alley or, if no alley is accessible, to a public street. Such spaces shall be provided with maneuvering and turning areas so that no vehicle will be required to back into a street, and shall be equal in area to at least the minimum requirements for the specific use with which associated as set forth below. 

 
(Code 2002, § 34-163; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 10.3) 
Sec. 38-199. - Continuing character of obligation. 
Required off-street parking and loading spaces associated with newly erected or altered buildings or newly established uses of land shall be a continuing obligation of the owner of said building or land, so long as the structure or use exists or its use requiring vehicle parking or vehicle loading facilities continues. It shall be unlawful for said owner to change the required vehicle parking or loading spaces apart from the discontinuance, sale or transfer of the building or use without establishing alternative vehicle parking or loading spaces which meet the requirements of, and are in compliance with, this article, or for any person to use a building or lot without providing vehicle parking or loading spaces which meet the requirements of, and are in compliance with, this article. 
(Code 2002, § 34-164; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 10.4) 
Secs. 38-200—38-221. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IX. - NONCONFORMING USES 

Sec. 38-222. - Applicability. 
In order to avoid individual hardship whenever reasonable and not in conflict with the general welfare of the city, the provisions of this article apply to all zoning districts. 
(Code 2002, § 34-191; Ord. of 2-10-2003, art. IX) 
Sec. 38-223. - Continuance. 
The lawful use of any building or lot existing at the time of the enactment of this article may be continued, except as hereafter provided, although such use does not conform to the provisions of this article. 
(Code 2002, § 34-192; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 11.1) 
Sec. 38-224. - Unsafe or unsanitary buildings. 
Any building or portion thereof declared unsafe or unsanitary by a proper authority shall be governed by the ordinance concerning unsafe buildings. 
(Code 2002, § 34-193; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 11.2) 
Sec. 38-225. - Restoration. 
No building damaged by fire or other causes to the extent of more than 50 percent of its fair market value shall be repaired or rebuilt except in conformity with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 2002, § 34-194; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 11.3) 
Sec. 38-226. - Abandonment. 
Whenever a nonconforming use has been discontinued for a period of one year, such use shall not thereafter be re-established, and any future use shall be in conformity with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 2002, § 34-195; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 11.4) 
Sec. 38-227. - Change to another nonconforming use not allowed. 
No nonconforming use may be changed to another nonconforming use. 
(Code 2002, § 34-196; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 11.5) 
Sec. 38-228. - Changes. 
Once changed to a conforming use, no building or land shall be permitted to revert to a nonconforming use. 
(Code 2002, § 34-197; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 11.6) 
Sec. 38-229. - Enlargement. 
No nonconforming use shall be enlarged or extended in any way. 
(Code 2002, § 34-198; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 11.7) 
Sec. 38-230. - Discontinuance of nonconforming uses of land. 
Nonconforming uses of land shall be discontinued within five years from the date the ordinance from which this article is derived becomes effective, or within five years from the date the use becomes nonconforming, whichever is later, in the following situations: 
(1)  Where no buildings are used in connection with the principal use. 
(2)  Where the only buildings used are accessory or incidental to the principal use. 
(3)  Where the use is maintained in connection with a building originally constructed for a conforming use. 
(Code 2002, § 34-199; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 11.8) 
Secs. 38-231—38-253. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE X. - EXCEPTIONS AND MODIFICATIONS 

Sec. 38-254. - Lot of record. 
In any residential zoning district where the owner of a lot existing at the time of the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived, or his successor in title thereto, does not own sufficient land to enable him to conform to the minimum lot area or frontage requirements of this article, such lot may be used for a one-family dwelling, provided that minimum yard and building setback requirements for the zoning district in which said lot is located are maintained. 
(Code 2002, § 34-221; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 12.1) 
Sec. 38-255. - Combination of adjoining and vacant lots of record. 
If two or more adjoining and vacant lots with continuous frontage are in a single ownership at any time after the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived, and such lots individually are less than the lot width requirements for the zoning district in which they are located, such groups of lots shall together be considered as a single lot, or shall be grouped into several lots of minimum permitted size, and the resulting lot or lots shall be subject to the dimensional requirements of this article. 
(Code 2002, § 34-222; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 12.2) 
Sec. 38-256. - Reduction in building setback line. 
The building setback requirements of this article for dwelling shall not apply to any lot where the average existing building setback line on lots located wholly or in part within 200 feet on each side of such lot, within the same block and in the same zoning district, and fronting on the same side of the same street as such lot, is less than the minimum required building setback. In such cases, the minimum building setback on said lot may be equal to the average of the existing setbacks on the aforementioned lots, or not less than ten feet from the street right-of-way, whichever is greater. 
(Code 2002, § 34-223; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 12.3) 
Sec. 38-257. - Yards in group developments. 
More than one dwelling, institutional, commercial or industrial building may be located upon a lot in a zoning district where such a use would be permitted, but no such building shall encroach upon the front, side or rear yards required for any other building side. For dwellings, the open space between buildings shall not be less than 20 feet for one-story buildings, 30 feet when either building is a two-story building, 40 feet when either building is a three-story building, and 40 feet plus an additional ten feet for each story over three stories when either building is over three stories in height. The minimum dimension for the yard upon which any entrance or exit of a dwelling faces shall be 20 feet, and such space shall not be counted as a yard for any other building. 
(Code 2002, § 34-224; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 12.4) 
Secs. 38-258—38-277. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XI. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 38-278. - Enforcing officer. 
The provisions of this article shall be administered and enforced by the mayor and city council with the assistance of the building inspector or his designee. The building inspector's duties in this capacity shall include inspection of premises, and issuing building and occupancy permits for uses and buildings that meet the requirements of this and other ordinances of the city. 
(Code 2002, § 34-241; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 13.1) 
Sec. 38-279. - Building permits. 
Building permits shall be issued in accordance with the following provisions: 
(1)  Building permit required. It shall be unlawful to commence the excavation or filling of any lot for construction of any building, or to commence construction of any building, or to commence the moving or alteration of any building, or to commence the development of land for a use not requiring a building, until the building inspector or his designee has issued a building permit for such work. 
(2)  Issuance of building permit. In applying to the building inspector or his designee for a building permit, the applicant shall submit two copies of a dimensioned sketch or to-scale plan signed by the owner or his authorized agent, indicating the shape, size and location of the lot to be built upon, and the shape, size, heights, uses and location of the buildings to be erected, demolished, altered or moved, and of any buildings already on the lot, the number of dwelling units the building is designed to accommodate, if any, the setback lines of buildings or adjoining lots, and such other information concerning the lot or adjoining lots as may be essential for determining whether the provisions of this article and other ordinances of the city then in force are met. When all requirements have been met, the building inspector or his designee shall issue a building permit upon payment of any required fees, and shall retain one copy of the building permit and the sketch or plan. 
(3)  Refusal of building permit. If the sketch or plan submitted describes work which does not conform to the requirements of this article, the building inspector or his designee shall not issue a building permit, but shall return the sketch or plan to the applicant along with a signed refusal in writing. Such refusal shall state the reasons therefor, and shall cite the portions of this article with which the submitted sketch or plan does not comply. The building inspector or his designee shall retain one copy of the sketch or plan and of the refusal. 
(4)  Time limitations. Any building permit issued shall become invalid unless the work authorized by it shall have been commenced within six months of its date of issue, or if the work authorized by it is suspended or abandoned for a period of one year. 
(Code 2002, § 34-242; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 13.2) 
Sec. 38-280. - Certificate of occupancy. 
Certificates of occupancy shall be issued in accordance with the following provisions: 
(1)  Certificate of occupancy required. Certificates of occupancy issued by the building inspector are required in advance of occupancy or use of: 
a.  A building hereafter erected. 
b.  A building hereafter altered. 
c.  A change of use of any building or lot. 
(2)  Issuance of certificate of occupancy. The building inspector shall sign and issue a certificate of occupancy if the proposed use of a lot or a building, as stated on the occupancy permit and signed by the owner or his appointed agent, is found to conform to the applicable provisions of this article and if the building, as finally constructed, complies with the sketch or plan submitted for the building permit. One copy of all certificates of occupancy issued, which contain a statement of the intended use of the applicable property signed by the owner or his agent, shall be kept on file in the office of the building inspector. Copies shall be furnished on request to any person having a proprietary or tenancy interest in the building or lot involved, at said person's expense. 
(3)  Denial of certificate of occupancy. A certificate of occupancy shall not be issued unless the proposed use of a building or lot conforms to the applicable provisions of this article, or unless the building as finally constructed complies with the sketch or plan upon which the building permit was issued, and otherwise conforms to the provisions of this article. 
(Code 2002, § 34-243; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 13.3) 
Sec. 38-281. - Records. 
It shall be the duty of the building inspector or his designee to keep a record of all building permits and occupancy permits issued, with a notation of all special conditions involved. He shall file and safely keep copies of all sketches and plans submitted, and the same shall form a part of the records of his office and shall be available for the use of the city council, the board of zoning appeals, the planning commission and other officials of the city. 
(Code 2002, § 34-244; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 13.4) 
Sec. 38-282. - Penalties. 
Any person violating a provision of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished for each violation according to law. Each day such violation continues shall be deemed a separate offense. 
(Code 2002, § 34-245; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 13.5) 
Sec. 38-283. - Remedies. 
In case any building is created, constructed, reconstructed, altered, repaired, converted or maintained, or any building or lot is used in violation of this article, the building inspector, or any other appropriate city authority, or any person who would be damaged by such violation, in addition to other remedies, may institute injunction, mandamus or other appropriate action in proceeding to prevent such violation in the case of each such building or use. 
(Code 2002, § 34-246; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 13.6) 
Secs. 38-284—38-314. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XII. - ZONING BOARD OF APPEALS 

Sec. 38-315. - Establishment. 
The city council may from time to time establish a board of appeals, as needed. Said board shall consist of three members appointed by the mayor and city council. Any vacancy shall be filled for the unexpired term in the same manner as the initial appointments. None of the members shall hold any other public office or position in the county, except that one member shall also be a member of the city planning commission. 
(Code 2002, § 34-271; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 14.1) 
Sec. 38-316. - Procedure. 
The board of appeals shall elect a chairperson from its membership who shall serve for one year or until he is re-elected or his successor is elected. The board of appeals shall appoint a secretary who may be an officer of the governing authority or a member of the planning commission. The board of appeals shall adopt rules in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(1)  Meetings of the board shall be held at the call of the chair, and at such other times as the board may determine. The chair or, in his absence, the acting chair, may administer oaths and compel the attendance of witnesses. All meetings shall be open to the public. 
(2)  The board shall keep minutes of its proceedings, showing the vote of each member upon each question or, if absent, or failing to vote, indicating such fact, and shall keep records of its examinations and other official actions, all of which shall be immediately filed in the office of the board and shall be a public record. 
(Code 2002, § 34-272; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 14.2) 
Sec. 38-317. - Appeals; how taken. 
Appeals to the board may be taken by any person aggrieved or by an officer, department, board or bureau of the governing authority affected by any decision of the administrative officer. Such appeals shall be taken within a reasonable time, as provided by the rules of the board of appeals, by filing with the officer from whom the appeal is taken, and with the board of appeals, a notice of appeal specifying the grounds thereof. The officer from whom the appeal is taken shall forthwith transmit to the board all papers constituting the record upon which the action was taken. 
(Code 2002, § 34-273; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 14.3) 
Sec. 38-318. - Stay of proceedings. 
An appeal stays all legal proceedings in furtherance of the action appealed from, unless the officer from whom the appeal is taken certifies to the board of appeals, after the notice of the appeal shall have been filed with him that, by reason of facts stated in the certificate, a stay would, in his opinion, cause imminent peril of life and property. In such case, proceedings shall not be stayed otherwise than by a restraining order that may be granted by the board of appeals or by a competent court. 
(Code 2002, § 34-274; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 14.4) 
Sec. 38-319. - Notice. 
The board shall fix a reasonable time for the hearing of the appeal or other matters referred to it, and give at least 15 days' public notice thereof by advertisement at least once in a newspaper of general circulation, as well as due notice to the parties in interest, and decide the same within a reasonable time. Upon a hearing, any party may appear in person or by agent or attorney. The foregoing provisions for notice shall apply to requests for variance, special exceptions and appeals of error which are hereinafter provided for in section 38-320. 
(Code 2002, § 34-275; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 14.5) 
Sec. 38-320. - Requests for variance, special exception or appeal of error. 
Requests for variance, special exception or appeal of error shall be filed in writing with the building inspector or his designee. Within ten days after receiving a request for variance, the building inspector or his designee shall: 
(1)  Send the request, with any comments he may deem necessary added thereto, to the board of zoning appeals or, if one has not been established, the city council; and 
(2)  Cause to have posted in a conspicuous place on the property one or more signs at the expense of the person from whom the appeal is taken. Each sign shall be not less than 12 square feet in area, and each of which shall contain information as to the proposed change and the date and time of the public hearings before the board of zoning appeals or city council. Such time shall be not less than 15 days after the posting of such sign or signs. 
(Code 2002, § 34-276; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 14.6) 
Sec. 38-321. - Powers. 
The board of zoning appeals, or, in its absence, the city council, shall have the following powers: 
(1)  Administrative review. To hear and decide appeals where it is alleged there is an error in any order, requirement, permit, decision, determination or refusal made by an administrative officer in the enforcement of this article. 
(2)  Variances. To authorize upon appeal in specific cases such variances from the terms of this article as will not be contrary to the public interest where, owing to special conditions, a literal enforcement of the provisions of this article will, in an individual case, result in a practical difficulty or unnecessary hardship, so that the spirit of the regulation shall be observed, public safety and welfare secured, and substantial justice done. Such variance may be granted in individual cases of practical difficulty or unnecessary hardship upon a finding by the board that all of the following exist: 
a.  There are extraordinary and exceptional conditions pertaining to the particular piece of property in question because of its size, shape or topography; 
b.  The application of this article to this particular piece of property would create practical difficulty or unnecessary hardship; and 
c.  Relief, if granted, would not cause substantial detriment to the public good or impair the purposes and intent of this article. However, no variance may be granted for a use of land or buildings or structure that is prohibited by this article. 
(3)  Exceptions. To hear and decide special exceptions to the terms of this article upon which such board of appeals is required to pass under. 
(Code 2002, § 34-277; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 14.7) 
Sec. 38-322. - Decision-making function. 
In exercising the above powers, the board of zoning appeals or city council may, in conformity with the provisions of this article, reverse or affirm, wholly or partly, or may modify the order, requirements, decision or determination, and to that end shall have all the powers of the officer from whom the appeal is taken and may issue and direct the issuance of a permit. 
(Code 2002, § 34-278; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 14.8) 
Sec. 38-323. - Appeal from decision. 
Any person or persons severally or jointly aggrieved by any decision of the board of zoning appeals or city council, may take an appeal to the superior court. Said appeal to the superior court shall be the same as an appeal to the superior court from any decision made by the court of the ordinary and as specified in O.C.G.A. title 5, ch. 4, except, however, that said appeal must be filed within 30 days from the date of the decision of the board of zoning appeals. Upon failure to file said appeal within 30 days, the decision of the board of zoning appeals shall be final; provided, however, that on appeal said case shall be heard by the judge of the superior court without a jury trial within 30 days from the filing of the appeal. 
(Code 2002, § 34-279; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 14.9) 
Secs. 38-324—38-349. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XIII. - AMENDMENTS 

Sec. 38-350. - Authority to amend. 
(a)  The mayor and council may from time to time amend any article or section of this chapter by adopting an amendment to the zoning chapter which changes: 
(1)  The text of the zoning chapter to change the number, shape, boundary or area of any district, to amend any regulation pertaining to a zoning district or any procedure relating thereto; or 
(2)  By the adoption of an amendment to the zoning chapter which rezones property from one zoning classification to another zoning classification authorized by the zoning chapter. 
(b)  An amendment to the zoning chapter, whether for the purpose of amending the text of the zoning chapter or to rezone property from one zoning classification to another, shall be by adoption of an amendatory ordinance in accordance with the ordinance procedure set forth in the Charter and this Code. 
(Ord. of 7-9-2012(2), § 1(34-301)) 
Sec. 38-351. - Initiation of zoning amendments. 
(a)  An application to amend the zoning chapter to amend the zoning map and rezone property from one zoning classification to another zoning classification may be made by the mayor or any member of the council, or by any person, firm or corporation owning all or any part of the real estate covered by and included in such request for amendment. 
(b)  Any amendment to the zoning chapter other than to rezone property from one zoning classification to another zoning classification may be proposed only by the mayor or any member of the council. 
(c)  If an application to rezone property from one zoning classification to another zoning classification is defeated by the mayor and council, the same property may not be again considered for rezoning until the expiration of at least six months immediately following the defeat the rezoning by the local government. 
(Ord. of 7-9-2012(2), § 1(34-302)) 
Sec. 38-352. - Filing applications for amendment. 
All applications for amendment to the zoning chapter of the city shall be filed with the city clerk or his designee, and unless the application is made by the mayor or any member of the council, all fees required by the resolution or ordinances of the city shall be paid at the time of such filing. 
(Ord. of 7-9-2012(2), § 1(34-303)) 
Sec. 38-353. - Public hearing. 
At the public hearing required by law prior to the adoption of a zoning amendment, the mayor and council shall: 
(1)  Receive a report from the mayor as to any comments for or against the proposal received by the city and hear any comments from the city staff; 
(2)  Hear from the applicants for the rezoning; and 
(3)  Hear from the opponents to the rezoning. 
a.  Proponents of the proposed zoning amendment shall have a minimum of ten minutes for the presentation of data, evidence and opinions relating to the zoning decision and opponents of such proposed zoning decision shall have an equal minimum time period for presentation of opposition as required by O.C.G.A. § 36-66-5(a). 
b.  Any local government official (which shall be deemed to include any member of the mayor and council) shall make the disclosure of financial interest required by O.C.G.A. § 36-67A-2. Any applicant for rezoning action and any opponent of a rezoning action must file the disclosure report of campaign contributions required by O.C.G.A. § 36-67A-3. The disclosure required from an applicant for rezoning action shall be filed within ten days after the application for the rezoning action is first filed and any opponent must file the disclosure at least five calendar days prior to the first hearing by the mayor and council or any of its agencies. 
(Ord. of 7-9-2012(2), § 1(34-304)) 
Sec. 38-354. - Notice of hearing. 
(a)  At least 15 but not more than 45 days prior to the date of the public hearing, the city clerk or his designee shall cause to be published in a newspaper of general circulation within the corporate limits of the city a notice of the hearing which shall state the time, place and purpose of the hearing. If the proposed zoning amendment is to rezone property from one zoning classification to another zoning classification, the notice shall also include the location of the property and the present and proposed zoning classification of the property. 
(b)  If the proposed amendment is to rezone property from one zoning classification to another zoning classification, the city clerk or his designee shall cause a sign to be placed upon the property for which the rezoning is sought. Such sign shall be placed upon such property at least 15 but not more than 45 days prior to the public hearing. The sign shall have surface of not less than 16 inches in height and 20 inches in width and the printing thereon shall be black with a light background and the letters shall be at least 1½ inches tall. The sign shall be placed in a conspicuous location on the property and must be visible from at least one street upon which the property abuts or on the access to such property and shall state the proposed zoning amendment, the date of the public hearing and shall contain a telephone number to call for further information relating to such proposed rezoning. 
(c)  The sign placed in accordance with the provisions of subsection (b) of this section shall not be removed therefrom by any person, firm or corporation until at least 24 hours after the date scheduled for the public hearing or if the public hearing is postponed or rescheduled, not less than 24 hours after the rescheduled date of such hearing and then such removal shall be accomplished only by the city clerk or his designee. It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to demolish, tear down, obliterate or remove a sign placed upon property in the city for the purpose of giving notice of a public hearing on a proposed rezoning other than the city clerk or his authorized designee. Any person, firm or corporation who shall violate the provisions hereof shall upon conviction be punished by order of the city as provided in section 1-7. 
(Ord. of 7-9-2012(2), § 1(34-305)) 
Secs. 38-355—38-381. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XIV. - STANDARDS GOVERNING THE EXERCISE OF THE ZONING POWER 

Sec. 38-382. - Purpose. 
The purpose of the following standards are to set forth the factors which shall be considered by the city council in balancing the interest of promoting the public health, safety, morality and the general welfare against the right of individuals to the unrestricted use of their property. 
(Code 2002, § 34-331; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 16.1) 
Sec. 38-383. - Standards. 
The standards to be considered are: 
(1)  The existing uses and zoning of nearby property; 
(2)  The extent to which property values are diminished by the particular zoning restrictions; 
(3)  The extent to which the diminution of the property value of the zoned area promotes the health, safety, morals and general welfare of the public; 
(4)  The relative gain to the public as compared to the hardship imposed upon the individual property owner; 
(5)  The suitability of the subject property for the zoned purposes; 
(6)  The length of time the property has been vacant as presently zoned compared to the development and use of other property in the area; 
(7)  The consistency of the proposed use of the property with the overall land use plan of the city. 
(Code 2002, § 34-332; Ord. of 2-10-2003, § 16.2)
